# Network+ Quiz ŌĆö Full Version History

This file holds the complete release history. The most recent 11 releases stay inline in [CLAUDE.md](./CLAUDE.md) for quick scanning; everything older lives here.

| Version | Features Added |

| v4.71.0 | **Three more scenario tours authored** ŌĆö Site-to-Site IPsec VPN (4 steps), MPLS Carrier WAN (4 steps), SASE Architecture (4 steps). Fourth batch ŌĆö continuing the same data-only discipline. **Site-to-Site VPN** complements v4.70.0's Hybrid Cloud by showing the office-to-office variant: always-on tunnel between two firewall gateways over public internet, no client software on endpoints, ESP encapsulation + Phase 1 IKE / Phase 2 ESP parameter symmetry. Pedagogically important contrast with remote-access VPN (which has client software per user). **MPLS** teaches the carrier-WAN vocabulary that still dominates large-enterprise backbones: CE (Customer Edge) at your site, PE (Provider Edge) at the carrier, label switching at L2.5 inside the cloud (LER pushes label, LSR swaps, PE pops), MP-BGP L3VPN vs L2VPN/VPLS flavors, QoS classes (EF/AF/BE) pre-engineered per path. N10-009 1.7 names MPLS explicitly. **SASE** teaches the modern cloud-converged security architecture: SD-WAN + SWG + CASB + ZTNA + FWaaS delivered from cloud PoPs, inspection at the edge instead of backhaul to HQ, identity-centric zero-trust per-request verification. Exam distinction: SASE = architecture; SSE = security-only subset. Same narrative discipline as prior batches ŌĆö step durations 13ŌĆō17s calibrated to word count. **14 tours total** now authored (Home, DMZ, Enterprise, Branch Wireless, SD-WAN, Small Office, Hub-Spoke, Cloud VPC, Hybrid Cloud, Full Mesh, Point-to-Point, Site-to-Site VPN, MPLS, SASE) ŌĆö 87% of the scenario catalog. UAT: 4080 ŌåÆ **4093** (+13 v4.71.0 data assertions). Playwright: **79/79** green. Cache: `netplus-v4.71.0`. ~160 LOC in `app.js` + `tests/uat.js`. **67th ship**. |
| v4.70.0 | **Three more scenario tours authored** ŌĆö Hybrid Cloud / VPN (4 steps), Full Mesh WAN (4 steps), Point-to-Point / Leased Line (4 steps). Third batch of three ŌĆö same data-only discipline as v4.68.0 + v4.69.0. **Hybrid Cloud** teaches the most common cloud-migration pattern: on-prem datacenter Ōåö VPC via IPsec tunnel, emphasising the exam-critical fact that IPsec Phase 1 (IKE) + Phase 2 (ESP) parameters must match byte-for-byte between peers or the tunnel never comes up (N10-009 1.8 + 4.1 + 4.4). **Full Mesh** teaches the O(n┬▓) growth problem: 4 sites = 6 links, 10 sites = 45 links, 20 sites = 190 links ŌĆö why full mesh collapses economically past ~5 sites and when the one-hop-latency + any-single-link-loss tolerance is worth the cost. **Point-to-Point** teaches the foundational WAN: dedicated leased line (T1 1.544 Mbps / T3-DS3 ~45 Mbps / OC-3 ~155 Mbps / OC-48 ~2.5 Gbps), SLA-backed deterministic latency + guaranteed bandwidth, CSU/DSU signal conversion, no shared carrier fabric. Same narrative discipline as prior batches ŌĆö wide iso for intros + takeaways, closer framings for concept beats, step durations 13ŌĆō15s calibrated to word count at ~3 words/sec. **11 tours total** now authored (Home, DMZ, Enterprise, Branch Wireless, SD-WAN, Small Office, Hub-Spoke, Cloud VPC, Hybrid Cloud, Full Mesh, Point-to-Point) ŌĆö two-thirds of the scenario catalog. 5 remaining for future batches (MPLS, Multi-AZ, plus 3 others). UAT: 4067 ŌåÆ **4080** (+13 v4.70.0 data assertions). Playwright: **79/79** green. Cache: `netplus-v4.70.0`. ~130 LOC in `app.js` + `tests/uat.js`. **66th ship**. |
| v4.69.0 | **Three more scenario tours authored** ŌĆö Small Office (4 steps), Hub-and-Spoke (4 steps), Cloud VPC (4 steps). Second batch of three. **Small Office** bridges Home Network and Enterprise: flat-LAN behind a stateful firewall, no DMZ, no internal segmentation ŌĆö the SMB default. **Hub-and-Spoke** teaches the pre-SD-WAN classic: HQ center of gravity, every branch connects only to HQ (no branch-to-branch), backhauled internet + inter-branch latency as the three weaknesses SD-WAN fixes. Complements v4.68.0's SD-WAN tour by showing WHY it won. **Cloud VPC** teaches the 3-tier cloud layout: IGW (bidirectional internet for public subnet) vs NAT-GW (outbound-only for private subnet), public-vs-private routing rules, Security Groups (stateful, instance-level) vs NACLs (stateless, subnet-level). Same narrative discipline as prior batches ŌĆö wide iso for intros + takeaways, closer framings for concept beats, step durations 12ŌĆō16s. **8 tours total** now authored (Home, DMZ, Enterprise, Branch Wireless, SD-WAN, Small Office, Hub-Spoke, Cloud VPC) ŌĆö half the scenario catalog. UAT: 4055 ŌåÆ **4067** (+12 v4.69.0 data assertions). Playwright: **79/79** green. Cache: `netplus-v4.69.0`. ~130 LOC in `app.js` + `tests/uat.js`. **65th ship**. 8 scenarios remaining for future batches. |
| v4.68.0 | **Three more scenario tours authored** ŌĆö Enterprise w/ IDS + Load Balancer (5 steps), Branch Office w/ Wireless (4 steps), SD-WAN Network (4 steps). **Pure data ship** ŌĆö zero engine changes; the v4.66.0 sequencer + v4.67.0 timing/Previous-button fixes carry every new tour. **Enterprise tour** covers IDS-vs-IPS, load balancer HA, two-firewall defense-in-depth, and the N10-009 2.4+4.1+4.3 exam ties. **Branch Wireless** teaches autonomous-vs-lightweight APs, CAPWAP as the control-plane tunnel, WLC as the brain, seamless roaming. **SD-WAN** teaches hub-and-spoke fabric, mixed transports (MPLS + broadband + LTE), dynamic app-aware path selection, shift from static MPLS-only to controller-driven WAN. Camera uses wide iso for intros + takeaways, closer framings for concept steps. Step durations calibrated to body word count (12ŌĆō16s) matching the v4.67.0 reading-pace model. Five tours total now authored (Home Network, DMZ, Enterprise, Branch Wireless, SD-WAN) covering the most pedagogically impactful cluster: SOHO ŌåÆ segmentation ŌåÆ enterprise HA/monitoring ŌåÆ branch wireless ŌåÆ modern WAN. UAT: 4043 ŌåÆ **4055** passing (+12 v4.68.0 data assertions). Playwright: **79/79** (no new E2E ŌĆö tours are data-only). Cache: `netplus-v4.68.0`. ~170 LOC in `app.js` + `tests/uat.js`. **64th ship**. Remaining scenarios (Small Office, Point-to-Point, Hub-and-Spoke, MPLS, Cloud VPC, Multi-AZ, Hybrid Cloud) are future data-only ships. |
| v4.67.0 | **Tour UX iteration + second authored tour (DMZ)**. Same-day ship after v4.66.0 Phase 4 landed. User feedback: step auto-advance felt "a tad fast" on the Home Network tour + no way to go back a step to re-read. **(1) Longer step durations** ŌĆö Home Network tour durations rewritten to match body word counts at ~3 words/sec reading pace + 2s visual-absorb buffer: Step 1 (35 words) 6.5s ŌåÆ 11s; Step 2 (42 words) 7.5s ŌåÆ 13s; Step 3 (35 words) 8s ŌåÆ 12s; Step 4 (52-word NAT takeaway) 9s ŌåÆ 15s. Longest body gets the longest step. **(2) Previous button** (ŌÅ«) added to tour playback controls between Pause and Skip. New `tb3dTourPrev()` in app.js: decrements `currentStep`, sets `playing = false` (auto-pauses so the user has unlimited time to re-read without the tour skipping forward again), re-renders the previous step with camera re-tween + device re-highlight. No-op if already at step 0. Users resume forward via the Resume button. **(3) DMZ / Screened Subnet tour authored** ŌĆö 5 steps, freeform narrative: Welcome (zones intro, wide iso) ŌåÆ The perimeter (dual-homed firewall, highlights Internet + FW) ŌåÆ The DMZ (containment concept, "attacker is trapped" ŌĆö longest step at 17s, highlights DMZ-SW + web + FTP) ŌåÆ The trusted inside (internal endpoints separated, internalŌåÆDMZ traffic still traverses the firewall) ŌåÆ Remember for the exam (public-facing server on LAN = red flag, screened-subnet = DMZ, segmentation + defense-in-depth). **UAT**: 11 new v4.67.0 assertions (tb3dTourPrev shape + no-op guard + HTML wiring + new duration thresholds + DMZ tour existence + 5 expected titles + longest-body Ōēź15s). Total UAT: 4032 ŌåÆ **4043** passing. Playwright: **79/79** green. Cache: `netplus-v4.67.0`. ~120 LOC across `index.html` + `app.js` + `tests/uat.js`. **63rd ship**. Second tour authored solidifies the pattern ŌĆö tours 3/4/5 are now pure data additions, no more engine work. |
| v4.66.0 | **Network Builder 3D View Mode ŌĆö Phase 4: Scenario Tours** (issue [#199](https://github.com/oremosu98/networkplus-quiz/issues/199) Phase 4). Each scenario can now carry a `tour: [...]` field that the 3D view plays as a choreographed camera + narrative sequence. First tour authored: **Home Network** (4-step freeform narrative ŌĆö Welcome ŌåÆ The internet edge ŌåÆ Wi-Fi and endpoints ŌåÆ Private IPs + NAT). Click **Ō¢Č Play Tour** in the 3D chrome ŌåÆ camera tweens through authored waypoints, captions fade in bottom-center, specific devices get accent-pulse rings on their labels. **Render-only architecture**: `tb3d.js` exports two new primitives ŌĆö `tweenCameraTo(position, target, durationMs)` (plain arrays so tour data is serializable) + `highlightDevices(hostnames)` (resolves by hostname since device IDs are runtime-generated). app.js owns all tour state (`_tbTourState` with active/tour/currentStep/playing/advanceTimer) + auto-advance timing. tb3d never mutates tour state. **Step shape**: `{title, body, camera:{position,target,durationMs}, highlight:[hostname...], durationMs}`. **Playback controls** in the chrome bar: Ō¢Č Play Tour (visible only when scenario has an authored `tour`); during playback swaps to ŌÅĖ Pause / Ō¢Č Resume / ŌÅŁ Skip / ├Ś Exit. Exit clears highlights + resets camera to INITIAL_CAM. **Caption card** bottom-center (680px max, pointer-events:none so orbit still works) with tour eyebrow + step title + step body + step-dot progress indicator. Fade-in animation per step change via forced `animation: none` + rAF trick. **Highlights** reuse Phase-2 packet-trace visual vocabulary but green-tinted (`.tb-3d-tour-highlight` + `@keyframes tb3dTourHighlightPulse`). Reduced-motion gate snaps camera instantly + kills caption fade + kills highlight pulse. **Home Network narrative** (6-9s per step) teaches the SOHO fundamentals: wide iso intro ŌåÆ pan to ISP+router for internet-edge concept ŌåÆ pan wider to show Wi-Fi + 4 endpoints ŌåÆ zoom out + highlight router alone for NAT takeaway. **UAT**: **24 new v4.66.0 assertions** ŌĆö 4 tb3d exports, 8 app.js wiring (state + 5 button delegates + step render + advance timer + exit cleanup + open/close hooks), 3 tour data checks, 3 HTML + 3 CSS, 2 regression guards (tb3d never touches `_tbTourState`, `Array.isArray(scen.tour)` invariant). Total UAT: 4009 ŌåÆ **4032** passing. Playwright: **79/79** still passing ŌĆö all 11 existing 3D E2E tests stay green under the extended state model. Cache: `netplus-v4.66.0`. ~550 LOC across `index.html` + `styles.css` + `tb3d.js` + `app.js` + `tests/uat.js`. **62nd ship** (v4.66.0 reuse ŌĆö the reverted polish pass freed this number). Closes Phase 4 of issue #199 for Home Network; additional tours (DMZ / Enterprise / Load Balancer) are authorable incrementally by adding `tour` fields to other `TB_SCENARIOS` entries. Phase 5 (3D drag/drop editing) remains deferred indefinitely. |
| v4.65.1 | **OSI Stack button UX patch** ŌĆö user reported the button stayed greyed out after loading a Home Network scenario in 3D view. v4.65.0 design required clicking a device in the 3D scene first (which selected it and enabled the OSI button) but there was no visible hint about that ŌĆö the disabled button just looked broken. **Three-part fix**: (1) removed `disabled` attribute from the OSI button in `index.html` so it's always clickable, (2) `tb3dEnterOsiView` now auto-picks a sensible device when nothing's selected ŌĆö preference: endpoint (pc/laptop/smartphone) ŌåÆ router ŌåÆ any non-cloud/isp-router ŌåÆ first device, (3) auto-picked device gets programmatically selected via `tbSelectDeviceForInspector` so the Live Inspector popup + OSI view open consistently. Tooltip rewritten from *"Show the selected device's 7-layer OSI stack"* ŌåÆ *"Explode a device into 7 OSI layers (clicks a device for you if none selected)"*. `_tb3dUpdateOsiButtonEnabled` kept as a safety no-op (only removes `disabled`, never adds it). `tbClose3DView` no longer re-adds disabled on 3D exit. **Lesson**: disabled-at-rest UX with no visible hint is a dead-UX trap ŌĆö if the remedy is "click something specific first", either auto-do the specific thing or make the hint unmissable. UAT assertion flipped: `v4.65.1 HTML: OSI button ships enabled` + `v4.65.1 REGRESSION: tb3dEnterOsiView auto-picks a device when none selected`. Playwright test now asserts first-click works with no prior selection. Total UAT: **4009 passing** (same count, updated names). Playwright: **79** passing. Cache: `netplus-v4.65.1`. ~30 LOC across `index.html` + `app.js` + `tests/uat.js` + `tests/e2e/app.spec.js`. **62nd ship**. Fourth same-day Friday ship. |
| v4.65.0 | **Network Builder 3D View Mode ŌĆö Phase 3** (issue [#199](https://github.com/oremosu98/networkplus-quiz/issues/199) Phase 3). Third feature ship of Friday, after Phase 1 (read-only explorer) + Phase 2 (packet trace). Adds the **OSI Layer Stack view** ŌĆö select any device, click ­¤ōČ OSI Stack, and the device "lifts" into a 7-plane exploded view showing every OSI layer (L1 Physical ŌåÆ L7 Application) with its PDU (Bits/Frame/Packet/Segment/Data) and typical protocols (Ethernet / IP / TCP / HTTP / etc.). This is the 2D-impossible teaching moment ŌĆö you cannot show the OSI stack spatially in a flat diagram. **Render-only architecture continues**: `tb3d.js` exports `enterOsiView(deviceId)` + `exitOsiView()`; app.js chrome buttons delegate; no new state owned by tb3d. **7 layered planes** ŌĆö translucent colored PlaneGeometry (L1 red ŌåÆ L7 purple matching CompTIA visual convention), stacked vertically 3.2 units apart above the focused device. Each plane has a CSS2DObject label attached to a dedicated anchor Object3D. **Anchor pattern discovered after 30-min debug**: directly attaching labels to the plane's rotated coordinate frame caused CSS2DRenderer's clip-space visibility check to silently fail on the first frame post-camera-tween; dedicated anchor with no rotation + `updateMatrixWorld(true)` + a 50ms post-creation forced `labelRenderer.render()` ensures the 7 label divs land in the DOM reliably. Vertical riser lines connect consecutive planes for stack continuity. **Non-focus devices dim to 20% opacity** (direct material.opacity mutation on every mesh in their group), cables drop to 18% so focus stays unambiguous. **Camera tween** frames the stack from an off-right angle; camera position + target backed up on enter, restored on exit. **OSI title card** (absolute-positioned top-center of chrome) shows device hostname + type + "click Exit OSI to return". **Chrome state machine**: OSI Stack button starts disabled (no selection); `tbSelectDeviceForInspector` fires `_tb3dUpdateOsiButtonEnabled` which flips `disabled`; entering OSI hides Trace + OSI Stack and reveals Exit OSI; exit reverses. `tbClose3DView` resets this state on 3DŌåö2D toggle so a second entry starts clean. **Resource cleanup** ŌĆö exitOsiView removes each label from its parent anchor BEFORE removing the anchor meshes, so the CSS2DObject `removed` event fires and its DOM element is properly detached. `tb3d.exit()` lifecycle defensively invokes `exitOsiView()` first if still active. **Layer colors**: L1 #ef6a7a ┬Ę L2 #f97316 ┬Ę L3 #f4c664 ┬Ę L4 #3fd28b ┬Ę L5 #2dd4bf ┬Ę L6 #6aa9f0 ┬Ę L7 #a99cff ŌĆö border-left on each label matching the plane's fill. **Reduced-motion gate** + **light-theme overrides**. **UAT**: **32 new v4.65.0 assertions** ŌĆö 13 tb3d module shape, 7 app.js wiring, 4 HTML, 5 CSS, 3 regression guards (OSI starts disabled, render-only invariant, exit() cleanup). Total UAT: 3977 ŌåÆ **4009** passing. Playwright: 75 ŌåÆ **79** passing (4 new: button enables on selection, 7 layers render on enter, Exit returns + tears down, Back-to-2D cleans up). Cache: `netplus-v4.65.0`. ~680 LOC across `tb3d.js` + `app.js` + `index.html` + `styles.css` + `tests/uat.js` + `tests/e2e/app.spec.js`. **61st ship**. **Third Friday feature ship** ŌĆö three 3D-view phases in one day. Closes Phase 3 of issue #199. Phase 4 (scenario 3D tours with camera choreography) queued. Phase 5 (3D drag/drop editing) remains deferred indefinitely. |
| v4.64.0 | **Network Builder 3D View Mode ŌĆö Phase 2** (issue [#199](https://github.com/oremosu98/networkplus-quiz/issues/199) Phase 2). Same-day Friday ship following Phase 1 from this morning. Brings the 3D view from read-only explorer to fully-narrative packet-trace playground ŌĆö click ­¤öŹ Trace, animate a glowing packet along real bezier cable curves hop-by-hop, watch MAC rewrites + TTL decrements happen in 3D space. **Render-only architecture**: all trace state stays in `_tbUiState.trace` (owned by `app.js` via existing v4.61.0 `tbStartTrace`/`tbTracePlay`/etc.); `tb3d.js` exports a new `setTraceState(traceState)` that app.js fires from a single hook-point inside `tbRenderTraceCanvasState()`. Zero state duplication, zero new mutation pathways, the 2D trace continues unchanged. Entering 3D mid-trace is continuous ŌĆö the HUD + hop strip pick up the existing state on `enter()`. **Glowing-packet animation**: yellow emissive SphereGeometry (0.28) + translucent glow sphere, animates along the `tbComputeTrace`-computed path using the Phase-1 cable bezier curves via `CubicBezierCurve3.getPoint(t)`. For hops with no physical cable between endpoints, falls back to `lerpVectors` straight-line animation. Reduced-motion gate jumps to destination. **Bottom hop-card strip** (160px, horizontal-scroll for long traces) ŌĆö one card per hop showing step number, color-coded layer chip (ARP/L3/DELIVER/FAIL), fromŌåÆto device, IP + interface + TTL detail, status pill (OK / BLOCKED / DELIVERED / PERMIT / FAIL). Cards flip from pending ŌåÆ current (accent-pulse + translate -3px) ŌåÆ done (green/red tint) as the packet moves. CSS `.tb-3d-host:has(.tb-3d-hop-strip:not([hidden]))` shrinks the canvas to make room ŌĆö matches the mockup. **Persistent trace HUD pill** top-right of chrome, animated accent-glow dot + `Packet Trace: ${srcHostname} ŌåÆ ${dstIp}`. **In-flight frame badge** ŌĆö CSS2DObject floating with the packet, shows layer + IPs + MAC rewrites + TTL before/after. Red variant for fail hops. **Playback controls** (hidden when no trace): Ō¢Č Play / ŌÅĖ Pause auto-swap, ŌÅŁ Step, 1├Ś speed cycles 1├Ś / 2├Ś / 0.5├Ś, ├Ś End. Buttons delegate to v4.61.0 `tbTracePlay/Pause/Step/EndTrace` via new `tb3dTrace*` wrapper fns. **Device-label ring states** ŌĆö visited green glow, current accent-pulse, pending dim 50%. Visited cables boost emissive 0.35 ŌåÆ 0.85. **2D trace panel auto-hide**: `tbOpen3DView` hides `#tb-trace-panel`; `tbClose3DView` restores it if trace still active ŌĆö prevents overlap. **UAT**: **33 new v4.64.0 assertions** ŌĆö 10 tb3d module shape, 9 app.js wiring, 4 HTML, 5 CSS, 1 reduced-motion gate, 3 regression guards (tbRenderTraceCanvasState persists, #tb-trace-panel persists, tb3d.js never mutates `_tbUiState` ŌĆö render-only contract locked). Total UAT: 3944 ŌåÆ **3977** passing. Playwright: 71 ŌåÆ **75** passing (4 new: DOM elements exist + hidden at rest, trace reveals HUD/strip/controls, trace state persists across 3DŌåö2D toggle, 2D panel hidden when 3D active). Cache: `netplus-v4.64.0`. ~720 LOC across `tb3d.js` + `app.js` + `index.html` + `styles.css` + `tests/uat.js` + `tests/e2e/app.spec.js`. **60th ship**. Closes Phase 2 of issue #199. | v4.63.0 | **Network Builder 3D View Mode ŌĆö Phase 1** (issue [#199](https://github.com/oremosu98/networkplus-quiz/issues/199)). | v4.62.0 | **Topology Builder ŌĆö Spanning Tree Protocol Visualisation** (issue [#186](https://github.com/oremosu98/networkplus-quiz/issues/186), **Phase 3 of TB v2 roadmap ŌĆö FINAL**). Concept-mockup-first again: drafted `~/Desktop/Dev Projects/tb-stp-viz-concept.html`; user *"perfect, lets build it"* ŌåÆ shipped same-day as the **4th feature of Wednesday**. STP auto-enables on every L2 switch ŌĆö no toggle. Add 2 switches + 2 cables between them ŌåÆ STP converges immediately, one port blocks automatically, no broadcast storm. **Pure function `tbComputeStpState(state)`** elects a root bridge by lowest bridge-ID (priority.MAC, default priority 32768), runs BFS over switch-to-switch cables to establish cost-to-root, then assigns port roles per cable endpoint: tree cables get `root` (child side) + `designated` (parent side); non-tree cables (would loop) get `designated` on the lower-bridge-ID side + `blocked` on the other. Non-switch endpoints get `null` role (hosts/routers don't participate). **Canvas overlay** (`tbRenderStpOverlay`): appends a `#tb-stp-layer` SVG group with (a) floating **­¤ææ crown** + "Root" label above the root bridge with gold pill background + tooltip, (b) **port-role dots** at every switch-to-switch cable endpoint ŌĆö gold root / green designated / red blocked, each with pedagogy tooltip, (c) **Ō£Ś badge** above blocked port dots, (d) **red dashed cable override** via `.tb-cable-stp-blocked` class on the conductor path ŌĆö `stroke-dasharray: 8 6` so the cable visibly fades to red-dashed while still being rendered (the "up but not forwarding" STP distinction). **Reconvergence pulse**: `tbRefreshStpState` diffs previous vs current port roles; switches whose role changed get a `.tb-stp-rethink` class for 800ms firing `tbStpRethink` keyframe (accent drop-shadow pulse), then the class clears. Root-change pulses ALL switches. **Hook into `tbSaveDraft()`**: every state mutation auto-recomputes + re-renders + pulses. `tbRenderCanvas` wrapped (composes with the v4.61.0 trace wrap via preserved wrapper flags). **MAC handling**: `_tbStpBridgeMac` uses first interface with a MAC, synthetic fallback from device id if none. **Scope OUT**: RSTP/MST, TCN, PortFast/BPDU Guard/Root Guard, PVST+, editable STP timers, dedicated build-a-loop scenarios (users can test on any topology with 2+ switches + redundant link), bridge-priority UI field (users can set `dev.stpPriority` via console or scenario seed ŌĆö proper UI field is v4.62.1 polish). **UAT**: **30 new v4.62.0 assertions** ŌĆö 8 structural, 8 CSS, and **14 behavioural vm-sandbox fixtures** on a 3-switch triangle asserting: converged flag true, SW-A elected root by lowest MAC tiebreaker, cost-to-root 0 for root / 1 for others, exactly 1 blocked port, tree cables forwarding (root/designated), non-tree cable blocks on lower-bridge-ID side (SW-B designated, SW-C blocked), priority override (`stpPriority = 4096` on SW-C) flips root to SW-C, empty topology returns converged+no-root, host-only topology has no STP election, mixed switch-host topology elects the single switch as root + cable gets null role on host-side. Each section renders an accent count badge when populated, a monospace table with hairline dotted row separators, and a friendly empty state ("ARP cache is empty ŌĆö no packets have flowed yet. Send a ping to populate.") when the table has no rows. Inapplicable sections (e.g. MAC table on a router, routing table on an L2 switch) render a monospace em-dash-prefix redirect stub ("Not applicable ŌĆö click a switch to see a MAC table") instead of hiding or showing zero-count noise, so users understand WHY a section is quiet. **Row-flash on insert**: module-level snapshot (`_tbInspPrevArpKeys` / `_tbInspPrevMacKeys`) diffed against the current ARP/MAC entries on every re-render ŌĆö new rows get `.tb-insp-row-flash` class + accent `box-shadow: inset 3px 0 0` rail + `tbInspRowFlash` keyframe (1800ms ease-out from `rgba(accent, .42)` ŌåÆ `rgba(accent, .18)`) + an inline `Learned` monospace pill in the Age cell. The snapshot resets when the inspected device changes so switching devices renders clean, no stale-flash carryover. **Live refresh** hooked into `tbSaveDraft()` ŌĆö every state mutation (ARP resolve, MAC learn, cable add, config edit) now re-renders the inspector if the popup is visible. Sending a ping and watching ARP populate = the money shot. ESC key closes the inspector (bound once at TB open via new `tbBindInspectorKeydown`, respects modal-layered state). Close button `├Ś` on the header already wired from v4.54.6. **Editorial head** matches the concept mockup: monospace small-caps eyebrow "INSPECTOR ┬Ę LIVE STATE" + accent-tinted gradient, 20px title with hostname, monospace sub showing `{type} ┬Ę N interfaces`. Open-full-config CTA at the footer preserves the double-click path to the editable config panel. **Helpers added**: `_tbRenderInspRouting(dev, flashKeys)`, `_tbRenderInspArp(dev, flashKeys)`, `_tbRenderInspMac(dev, flashKeys)`, `_tbRenderInspDhcp(dev)`, `_tbInspAccSection`, `_tbInspInapplicable`, `_tbInspEmpty`, `_tbInspRowClass`, `_tbInspEsc`, plus device-role predicates `_tbInspDeviceHasL3`, `_tbInspDeviceIsSwitch`, `_tbInspDeviceIsDhcpServer`. **Existing state shape reused** (no migration): `dev.routingTable` (pre-existing, rendered by old summary), `dev.arpTable` (populated by `_tbResolveArp` at app.js:17585 on every ARP request), `dev.macTable` (populated at line 17591 as packets flow through switches), `dev.dhcpServer` config object. Live DHCP lease tracking is NOT in the packet-sim engine today ŌĆö DHCP section shows static pool config + an honest note that live-lease tracking arrives in a future ship. **Scope OUT (deferred to v4.60.1/2)**: click-outside-to-close (could conflict with existing canvas patterns; ESC + ├Ś are the v1 close paths), device-move auto-dismiss (pinned during drag feels more intuitive), DHCP live-lease rows, per-hop packet trace (Phase 2), STP visualisation (Phase 3), CSV export, time-series history. **UAT**: **30 new v4.60.0 assertions** ŌĆö 11 structural (all 4 renderers defined, accordion/inapplicable/empty helpers defined, diff-set logic, `tbSaveDraft` refresh hook, ESC keydown binding, role predicates, editorial head markup), 5 CSS (accordion styles, row-flash keyframe, reduced-motion neutraliser, light-theme overrides, inapplicable + empty stub styling), and **15 behavioural vm-sandbox fixtures** extracting each renderer + helper function body and running them against realistic fixture data: ARP renderer with 2 entries + flashKey set emitting exactly 1 flashed row with `Learned` label, MAC renderer with 2 entries rendering vlan + port, routing renderer distinguishing connected (no next-hop) from static (with next-hop), DHCP renderer with pool config rendering network+range+gateway, DHCP renderer returning null on non-DHCP device (renderer contract), inapplicable stub rendering friendly message with redirect strong-highlight. | v4.59.7 | **Bug fix: home-page domain grid showed Service/Perf/Connection Issues as muted despite user having studied them** ŌĆö user screenshotted the "By Domain" grid with the Troubleshooting card circling Service Issues / Perf Issues / Connection Issues, all rendered with the muted-dot treatment reserved for topics not in the weak-spot set. User: *"these are greyed out even though ive already attacked these questions already."* **Root cause**: 5th read-path miss from the v4.57.4 multi-topic sentinel fix arc. `computeWeakSpotScores` at `app.js:8342` has a history loop (line 8378) that uses `e.topic` directly as a key: `touch(e.topic)` ŌåÆ `d.wCorrect += ...` / `d.wTotal += ...`. For pre-v4.57.1 multi-topic sessions saved with sentinel `"Multi: A, B, C"`, this creates a topicData entry under the nonsense sentinel key ŌĆö the real constituent topics get zero history credit. They then hit the low-signal filter (`wTotal < 1 && wrongsRecent < 0.5`) ŌåÆ excluded from weak-spot set ŌåÆ rendered as muted on the home grid, which the user reads as "never attacked". v4.57.4's release notes said weak-spot scoring was "NOT touched" because it "uses the per-question wrong-bank which has correct attribution" ŌĆö true for the wrong-bank loop (line 8362), **false for the history loop** (line 8378) which reads session-level `e.topic` and IS sentinel-affected. Honest miss; arc now closes at 5 read paths. **Fix**: added `_expandHistoryForWeakSpots(hist)` sibling helper next to `_filterHistoryByTopic` (same backward-compat rationale ŌĆö read-side only, no data migration, forward+backward compatible). Helper walks history and splits sentinel rows into N per-topic rows with score/total divided evenly across listed topics (sum invariant preserved); plain rows pass through unchanged. `computeWeakSpotScores` now routes `loadHistory().filter(...)` ŌåÆ `_expandHistoryForWeakSpots(rawHist)` ŌåÆ aggregate loop. User's exact scenario (15/20 multi-topic session with 3 topics) now credits 5/6.67 per topic at 75% posterior, triggering accuracy gap > 0 against the 0.85 target ŌåÆ topics surface as weak ŌåÆ accent-dot treatment on the grid. **Side effects**: Topic Progress, Knowledge Constellation, Domain drill-down, Study Plan, and weak-spot chip row all now agree on pre-v4.57.1 multi-topic study credit; the domain grid matches what those other surfaces showed post-v4.57.4. **UAT**: **24 new v4.59.7 assertions** ŌĆö 3 structure (helper defined, sentinel-split logic, `computeWeakSpotScores` routes through expander) + 14 behavioural vm-sandbox fixtures on the expander (3-topic split, plain passthrough, invariant preservation, defensive null/empty/no-topic cases, single-topic Multi: edge case) + 5 integration fixtures re-running `computeWeakSpotScores` sandbox with sentinel history and asserting Service/Perf/Connection Issues surface as weak rows + 2 regression tombstones (sentinel key itself must not appear as row, `computeWeakSpotScores` body must include the expander call). | v4.49.4 | **Grade + Coach refuse to run on pristine reference scenarios** \u2014 user asked *"i need a rule that if Scenario build is made, the Grade and Coach buttons shouldnt work for it since its Scenario Build rather than a build i did myself or ai generated"*. Reasoning: grading a reference topology against its own rules is trivially 100% \u2014 not pedagogically useful. | v4.49.2 | **Scenarios show green packets \u2014 zero blocked/red cables across 31 scenarios** \u2014 user flagged *"Red packets mean there is something wrong with the network configuration right? So how comes in almost all the scenarios, Labs, and AI generates networks there is red packets? Surely the red packets should only exist in the Fix a network activity."* User\u2019s mental model 100% correct. **Three distinct bugs compounded**: (1) `TB_NO_IP_NEEDED` had only 3 entries (switch/dmz-switch/cloud) \u2014 any scenario using WAPs, modems, cell-towers, satellites, SAN arrays, WLCs, ISP-routers, or cloud-logical nodes (VPC/subnet/IGW/NAT-GW/TGW/VPG/SASE/on-prem-DC) flagged those cables as blocked because those devices had no IPs; (2) `_tbMkCable` with default indices `(0, 0)` silently overwrote `cableId` on shared interfaces \u2014 multiple cables attached to the same hub router all wrote to `iface[0]`, leaving all but the last cable with severed interface references; (3) scenarios passing EXPLICIT `aIdx=1` hit interfaces already claimed by earlier auto-picked cables, same silent overwrite. **Fix \u2014 4 changes**: **(1) Expanded `TB_NO_IP_NEEDED`** from 3 to 18 types, organised by role: L2 bridges (switch, dmz-switch, wap), cloud + cloud-abstraction (cloud, vpc, cloud-subnet, igw, nat-gw, tgw, vpg, sase-edge, onprem-dc), transit/broadband/radio (modem, cell-tower, satellite, isp-router), storage fabric (san-array), wireless mgmt (wlc). **(2) Auto-assign link-local IPs** in `_tbMkCable` so any L3 interface without an IP gets one automatically: L3\u2194L3 pair gets matching `/30` link-local (`169.254.N.X` and `+1`); L3\u2194exempt gets a `/24` one-sided assignment on the L3 side (`169.254.10+N.X/24`). Matches RFC 3927 APIPA convention. Console cables skipped. **(3) `nextFreeIdx` + `resolveIdx` helpers** in `_tbMkCable`: when no explicit index passed, scan for first interface without a `cableId` (or create one); when explicit index clashes with an already-attached slot, fall forward to next free. Stops silent overwrites without requiring scenario authors to hand-track interface indices. **(4) `_tbLinkLocalSlot` counter reset** in `tbLoadScenarioWithBuild` before each autoBuild runs \u2014 deterministic IP assignments on scenario re-load. **Cable health scoring** itself unchanged \u2014 `fromHasIp = fromIfc?.ip || fromExempt` formula still works; we just widened "exempt" and filled more `ip`s. **Live-verified via Claude-in-Chrome MCP across all 31 scenarios**: 255 total cables tested via `tbAssessCableHealth(cable)`. Results: **232 flowing** (91%), **0 blocked** (was ~94 before fix), **23 degraded** (9%, concentrated in scenarios where subnets intentionally differ and routing would be needed \u2014 DSL/cable/FTTH with separate home+ISP subnets, point-to-point leased lines between different site networks, hub-spoke with per-branch subnets. These are **pedagogically correct amber** \u2014 "traffic works but needs a router to bridge"). | v4.45.1 | **Domain Mastery tier thresholds ŌĆö grounded in real CompTIA pass math** ŌĆö user disputed the v4.45.0 tier labels: at 70% they were marked "Developing" which they argued should be "Proficient." Analysis confirmed the dispute was right. **Why the original 60/75/85 was wrong**: picked for "clean even quartiles" and anchored to our linear scaled-score formula (`100 + raw ├Ś 800 = 720` gives 77.5% raw as pass). But real CompTIA N10-009 scoring is non-linear and form-specific; actual raw-accuracy pass equivalent is consistently cited at **~70ŌĆō75%**. So a user at 70% is already in the "probably passes today" zone \u2014 calling that "Developing" is both psychologically wrong (70% isn\u2019t still-learning-fundamentals, it\u2019s refining) and factually misaligned with the real exam. **New thresholds 55 / 70 / 85**: Novice <55% (was <60%) \u2014 "still learning fundamentals"; Developing 55\u201369% (was 60\u201374%); Proficient 70\u201384% (was 75\u201384%) \u2014 "you\u2019d likely pass the exam today"; Mastered \u226585% (unchanged, aspirational). Inline code comment in `tierInfo()` documents the dispute + reasoning so a future session doesn\u2019t revert without context. **Not changed**: the Readiness algorithm (separate composite of accuracy / coverage / recency / volume, still 420\u2013870 scaled) is untouched \u2014 this is a labeling refinement on the Domain Mastery card only. 85% mastery target-tick on the progress bar is also unchanged, so the aspirational ceiling still reads the same. **Snapshot effect on user\u2019s dashboard**: 4 of 5 domains flip from Developing \u2192 Proficient (1.0 at 70%, 2.0 at 71%, 4.0 at 74%, 5.0 at 75%). 3.0 at 78% stays Proficient. Only \u2264 54% would read as Novice under the new thresholds (user has no domain that low). **UAT**: 5 new v4.45.1 assertions \u2014 Proficient threshold now at 70% (regex against `pct >= 70) return { label: 'Proficient'`), Developing starts at 55%, Mastered still 85%, **regression guards** on the old 75% Proficient and 60% Developing cutoffs (must stay gone). Behavioural vm-sandbox smoke was drafted but dropped because the non-greedy `};\n` extraction regex truncated at the first return statement inside the arrow function; the 5 structural regex tests above give sufficient coverage without the brace-depth extraction gymnastics. Also updated the 2 existing version-string assertions (4.45.0 \u2192 4.45.1). Total UAT: 2572 \u2192 **2577** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. | v4.45.0 | **Analytics revamp ŌĆö Domain Mastery + Wrong-Answer Patterns replace Heatmap + Type Breakdown** ŌĆö user called out the old Difficulty ├Ś Topic Heatmap and Question Type Breakdown cards as low-value: *"these two statistics dont show me much value."* Analysis confirmed both were **descriptive without being prescriptive** (showed data but didn\u2019t drive action): the heatmap was a sparse matrix (most cells empty because you don\u2019t drill every topic at every difficulty) and the type breakdown had 3 of 5 rows with too-small sample sizes to mean anything (CLI Sim 4 attempts, Topology PBQ 1 attempt). Proposed 4 replacement candidates with an ROI analysis (A: Domain Mastery Ladder, B: Exam Pace Tracker, C: Wrong-Answer Patterns, D: Objective Coverage) \u2014 user picked **A + C**. **(1) Domain Mastery Ladder** (`_renderAnaDomainMastery`, full-width above the 2-col grid): 5 rows, one per N10-009 domain (Concepts 23% / Implementation 20% / Operations 19% / Security 14% / Troubleshooting 24%), each with a progress bar toward the 85% mastery threshold, a tier badge (Novice <60% / Developing 60-75% / Proficient 75-85% / Mastered 85%+), and a drill button. Progress bar includes a vertical 85% target tick so you can see at a glance how close each domain is. Each row has a left-border accent color matching the domain. Unstudied domains get a "Not started" state with a "Start drilling \u2192" button. Drill button fires new `drillDomain(domainName)` helper which finds the weakest topic in that domain (unstudied topics get priority via -1 sentinel) and pipes it into the existing `focusTopic()` flow \u2014 one click \u2192 targeted quiz starts. Data aggregates from `loadHistory()` via `TOPIC_DOMAINS` mapping, not from the weighted readiness computation \u2014 raw accuracy is the right metric for the "how close to 85%" question. **(2) Wrong-Answer Patterns** (`_renderAnaWrongPatterns`, inside the 2-col grid replacing Question Type Breakdown): clusters the last 20 entries from `loadWrongBank()` by signal and surfaces top 3\u20134 patterns: (a) **Negation traps** \u2014 stems containing NOT / EXCEPT / CANNOT / NEVER / LEAST / WORST; if \u22653 of last 20, flag "you're reading past the trap word"; (b) **Dominant domain cluster** \u2014 the N10-009 domain with the most wrongs, if \u22653; gets a drill button to jump into that domain; (c) **PBQ structure issues** \u2014 multi-select or order wrongs combined \u22652; tailored coaching depending on which dominates ("Choose TWO" miss vs sequence misread); (d) **Hard-difficulty concentration** \u2014 if \u22654 of last 20 are Hard-tier, suggests dropping back to Exam-Level until solid. Each pattern renders as a card with: numbered rank badge, icon, title, count \u00b7 pct, coaching copy, and a drill button where applicable. If no pattern meets its threshold the card renders a positive empty state ("your recent wrongs are scattered \u2014 no single failure mode dominates"). **Layout change**: Domain Mastery is promoted OUT of the 2-col grid to full-width because it\u2019s the most prescriptive card on the page and deserves the space. Wrong-Answer Patterns takes the grid slot where the heatmap used to live. The grid now holds: Streak, Weak Spots, Wrong-Answer Patterns, Exam-vs-Quiz. **What\u2019s NOT in this ship** (deferred from the 4-candidate menu): B (Exam Pace Tracker \u2014 most novel but requires new time-tracking aggregation) and D (Objective Coverage \u2014 very granular, can tuck inside Domain Mastery as an expandable later). Could slot into v4.46 if you want them. **CSS**: brand-new `.dm-*` rule set (27 declarations) and `.wp-*` rule set (14 declarations); old `.ana-heatmap`, `.ana-heat-*`, `.ana-type-*` rules deleted. Light-theme overrides added for both new cards. Progress bar uses `transition: width 800ms cubic-bezier(0.2, 0.8, 0.2, 1)` for smooth initial fill. 85% target line is a 2px absolute-positioned div with `transform: translateX(-50%)` for pixel-perfect centering on the threshold. **UAT**: 19 new v4.45.0 assertions \u2014 both new functions defined, `drillDomain` wires to `focusTopic(target)`, `renderAnalytics` call sites updated, **regression guards** on the old `_renderAnaHeatmap` + `_renderAnaQuestionTypes` functions (must stay gone) AND the old call sites in `renderAnalytics`, all 4 tier-badge CSS classes present, `.dm-bar-fill` 800ms cubic-bezier transition, `.dm-bar-target` positioned at 85%, `.wp-pattern` + rank/count CSS present, old `.ana-heatmap` + `.ana-type-list` CSS gone (regression guards), all 5 N10-009 domain IDs referenced in the Domain Mastery data, Wrong-Pattern classifier covers all 4 pattern categories. | v4.43.9 | **Release-flow hygiene ŌĆö `bump-version.js` now prepends to CLAUDE.md top (eliminates Read/Edit race)** ŌĆö user flagged repeated CLAUDE.md hiccups over the session: *"make sure that stays regularly updated. I dont want any excuses or hiccups there. High quality always."* The root cause was a flaw in `scripts/bump-version.js`: it was scanning for the LAST version row and inserting AFTER it (bottom of the table). The convention, established in the v4.42.3-audit reorg, is newest-first. So every release required a manual "move stub row from bottom to top, expand into full detail" Edit after running the bump script. That Edit consistently hit `"File has been modified since read"` errors because the bump script had mutated CLAUDE.md between my earlier Read and the later Edit. Work-around was a docs-only follow-up commit per release, which is sloppy and leaves the code+docs commit incomplete. **Fix ŌĆö `scripts/bump-version.js` now prepends** by finding the FIRST version row and inserting immediately before it. That puts the new row right under the `|---|---|` header (the correct position for newest-first). No "move row" Edit needed anymore ŌĆö the stub is already at the top; a single in-place expansion Edit is all that\u2019s required, and that Edit is against a file state freshly re-Read after the bump (not a stale pre-bump snapshot). **Release-flow discipline documented in CLAUDE.md** under the Deployment > Version bumps section: (1) run `bump-version.js` first, (2) **Read CLAUDE.md again** before the stub-expansion Edit (the bump script mutated it; any pre-bump Read snapshot is stale), (3) expand in place \u2014 no move required, (4) UAT \u2192 commit \u2192 push, all in one commit, no trailing docs-only follow-up. **UAT**: 6 new v4.43.9 regression guards \u2014 script\u2019s new comment header *"prepend to version history table"* present (pins the intent), script looks for FIRST `/^\| v\d/` match (not last), uses `lines.splice(firstVersionIdx, 0, newRow)` (prepend not append), success log says *"added at top"*, **regression guards** that the old "Find the last version row and insert after it" comment is gone AND the old `lastVersionIdx + 1` splice pattern is gone. Also updated the 2 existing version-string assertions (4.43.8 \u2192 4.43.9). This release itself is the proof \u2014 the stub landed at line 308 (top of table) automatically; this expansion Edit ran cleanly with zero file-state errors; single commit shipping both tooling fix and docs update. **No production code changes \u2014 tooling + docs only.** UAT: 2528 \u2192 **2534** passing. | v4.43.8 | **Smallest-satisfying-subnet guard ŌĆö rejects wasteful subnet-sizing answers** ŌĆö user hit a Hard subnet-sizing question: *"assigns 10.50.0.0/16 \u2014 5 subnets with at least 4,000 usable hosts each \u2014 which mask?"* Options: /19 (8190 usable, 8 subnets) ┬Ę /20 (4094 usable, 16 subnets) ┬Ę /21 (2046) ┬Ę /18 (only 4 subnets). Haiku marked **/19** claiming "more headroom is better." User correctly disputed: **/20 is the right answer** \u2014 it satisfies both constraints (\u22654,000 hosts, \u22655 subnets) with minimum waste. CompTIA convention is *smallest-satisfying-subnet wins* \u2014 this class of question tests whether you pick the efficient mask, not the most spacious one. Neither `_groundTruthOk` nor the unique-word check rejected it because nothing is factually wrong \u2014 /19 is valid, just sub-optimal. **Fix \u2014 new `_smallestSubnetOk(q)` guard at `app.js:4817`** (~70 lines, wired into `validateQuestions` alongside `_numericOptionOk`): **(1) Activation gate** \u2014 only triggers on MCQ questions whose stem contains a sizing phrase (`at\s+least` / `minimum` / `requires` / `needs` / `must\s+support`) paired with `hosts?|devices?|endpoints?|users?|addresses?`, AND explicitly asks for a subnet mask / CIDR / prefix. Anything else short-circuits to `true` (don\u2019t interfere). **(2) Constraint extraction** \u2014 pulls host-count requirement (numeric, comma-tolerant: `4,000` \u2192 4000), optional subnet-count requirement (`5 subnets|departments|networks|sites|vlans|offices|branches|segments`), and optional parent CIDR gated by assignment language (`assigns?|allocated?|assigned|receives?|given|uses?|has|owns?`) to avoid capturing a random `/N` that appears mid-stem as an example. **(3) Option parsing** \u2014 each A/B/C/D option parsed as a CIDR: prefer explicit `/N`, fall back to dotted-quad mask by counting 1-bits (valid range 0-32). If ANY option can\u2019t be parsed, the guard bails (`return true`) rather than producing a false positive. **(4) Satisfaction check** \u2014 an option satisfies if `usable = 2^(32-cidr) - 2 >= hostReq` AND (when parent + subnet-count constraints are both present and parent is a valid ancestor) `2^(cidr - parentCidr) >= subnetReq`. **(5) Decision**: 0 satisfying \u2192 return true (premise is broken, let other layers catch); 1 satisfying \u2192 must equal the marked answer; 2+ satisfying \u2192 the marked answer must be the one with the largest CIDR value (= smallest subnet, least waste). **Regression fixtures (`tests/validation-audit.js`)**: corpus expanded 20 \u2192 23 with 3 new cases pinning the behavior. **#21** is the exact user bug (parent /16, 5 subnets, 4,000 hosts, marked /19 when /20 is smallest-satisfying) \u2014 `shouldBeCaught: true`, **guard catches it**. **#22** is a single-satisfying control (only /19 provides \u22658,000 hosts; marked /19) \u2014 `shouldBeCaught: false`, guard activates and passes. **#23** is a non-sizing subnet question (*"what is the network address for X/26"*) \u2014 `shouldBeCaught: false`, guard\u2019s sizingRe short-circuits, no-op. Audit result: catch rate **62.5% \u2192 64.7%** (11/17 broken caught), false-positive rate **still 0%** (6/6 good kept). Regression gate (`MIN_CATCH_RATE = 60`, `MAX_FP_RATE = 0`) passed. **UAT**: 11 new v4.43.8 assertions \u2014 `_smallestSubnetOk` defined at module scope, body extracted for scoping, sizingRe covers all 5 host-synonyms, usable-host formula uses `Math.pow(2, 32 - cidr) - 2` exactly, subnet-count constraint applies `Math.pow(2, cidr - parentCidr)` only when `parentCidr < cidr`, option parsing supports both `/N` and dotted-mask fallback (`toString(2).match(/1/g)`), largest-CIDR selection via `cidrs[L] > cidrs[bestLetter]`, guard wired into `validateQuestions` with the exact `if (!_smallestSubnetOk(q)) return false` call, validation-audit stub includes `smallestSubnetSrc` extraction. Plus **2 behavioural smoke tests** \u2014 extract the helper into a `vm` sandbox, feed the user\u2019s exact fixture with `answer: 'A'` (expects `false` = reject) then with `answer: 'B'` (expects `true` = pass). Also updated the 2 existing version-string assertions (4.43.7 \u2192 4.43.8). Total UAT: 2517 \u2192 **2528** passing. Validation-audit regression gate green at 64.7%. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.43.8`. |

| v4.43.5 | **Exam-mode validation parity ŌĆö same 4-layer pipeline + graceful degradation banner** ŌĆö user-raised follow-up to v4.43.4 after noting the quiz-mode validation fix didn't apply to the 90-question exam simulator. Code audit confirmed: `startExam()` was shipping raw Haiku output concatenated across 5 batches of 18 with **zero validation** ŌĆö no Sonnet semantic pass, no programmatic `validateQuestions` (with GT tables / keyword / numeric-option / reported-question guards). At 10ŌĆō40% typical validation dropout, 9ŌĆō36 of 90 exam questions could carry quality issues into the real simulator, poisoning (a) exam score (wrong-marked broken questions), (b) Readiness Score (exam attempts weighted 1.3├Ś), (c) trust in the simulator vs the real CompTIA. **Fix ŌĆö same pipeline as startQuiz, scaled to exam batches**: **(1) Constants**: `EXAM_BATCH_BASE = 18`, `EXAM_BATCH_BUFFER = 5` (~28% per-batch buffer). Initial generation: (18+5) ├Ś 5 = 115 for 90 delivered. **(2) Per-batch validation**: each batch runs through `aiValidateQuestions(key, rawBatch)` (Sonnet) then `validateQuestions(aiValidated)` (programmatic GT/keyword/numeric). Same 62.5% programmatic catch + Sonnet's semantic catch as quiz mode, regression-gated by `tests/validation-audit.js`. **(3) Per-batch retry-to-fill**: if `batch.length < EXAM_BATCH_BASE` after validation, fetch `deficit + EXAM_BATCH_BUFFER` more, validate, concat. ONE retry per batch (not a loop ŌĆö cost-bounded). Wrapped in try/catch with `console.warn` so a transient API blip doesn't kill the whole exam. **(4) Slice + defensive final slice**: `batch.slice(0, EXAM_BATCH_BASE)` before concat; defensive `examQuestions.slice(0, EXAM_QUESTION_COUNT)` after injectPBQs. **(5) Graceful degradation banner (user direction: Option B)**: if final count < 90 after all batches + retries (rare ŌĆö both rounds dropped heavily), exam still ships. New `showExamShortfallBanner(actualCount)` helper prepends a dismissible amber info banner to `#page-exam`: *"This exam has N of 90 questions ŌĆö M were filtered out by the quality validator. Your score scales against the actual count, so the 720 pass mark stays accurate."* Scaling formula `Math.round(100 + (correct/total) ├Ś 800)` uses `total = examQuestions.length`, so 68/85 Ōēł 740 same as 72/90. **UX during load**: per-batch labels show 3 states ŌĆö "Batch 3 / 5 ŌĆö generatingŌĆ”" ŌåÆ "Batch 3 / 5 ŌĆö verifyingŌĆ”" ŌåÆ (if retry) "Batch 3 / 5 ŌĆö filling 4 moreŌĆ”". | v4.43.4 | **Question-count bug fix ŌĆö quizzes now always ship the qCount you picked** ŌĆö user-reported bug via Recent Performance screenshot showing consistent under-delivery: a 10-question selection yielded 7/9, 4/8, 5/9, 4/7 across recent sessions (total ŌēĀ 10). Root cause was in `startQuiz()` around line 1407: the pipeline asked Haiku for *exactly* `qCount` questions, then the 4-layer validation stack (prompt self-check ŌåÆ `aiValidateQuestions` ŌåÆ `validateQuestions` ŌåÆ `_groundTruthOk`) typically dropped 10ŌĆō40%, and the retry logic **silently accepted the shortfall** as long as it was Ōēź qCount/2 (comment: `// Acceptable shortfall ŌĆö validation removed some; continue with what we have`). Only if dropout was severe (>50%) did it retry. That was wrong ŌĆö the user explicitly picked 10, should always get 10. **Fix**: replaced the accept-shortfall branch with an **over-request + retry-to-fill** pattern. **(1) Over-request at initial fetch**: new `DROPOUT_BUFFER = Math.max(3, Math.ceil(qCount * 0.3))` ŌĆö 30% buffer with a min of 3 to cover small-N cases (qCount=5 ŌåÆ +3, qCount=10 ŌåÆ +3, qCount=20 ŌåÆ +6). Initial `fetchQuestions(key, topic, diff, qCount + DROPOUT_BUFFER)` pulls 13 from Haiku for a 10-q quiz; after Sonnet validator + programmatic `validateQuestions`, typical landing is 10ŌĆō12 remaining. **(2) Retry-to-fill if still short**: if `questions.length < qCount` after validation, compute `deficit = qCount - questions.length` and fetch `deficit + DROPOUT_BUFFER` more from Haiku, run through the same validation pipeline, concat. This is ONE retry, not a loop ŌĆö keeps cost bounded even in pathological cases. **(3) Retry wrapped in try/catch**: if the retry fetch fails (API hiccup, network blip), ship what we have rather than erroring out ŌĆö partial quiz is always better than a hard failure. `console.warn` logs the retry failure for observability. **(4) Final slice**: truncates any overage down to exact `qCount`. If still short after retry (both generations dropped heavily ŌĆö rare on niche topics), ship what we have. **User-facing behavior**: loading message on retry is *"Generating N more to complete your qCount-question setŌĆ”"* so the user sees the pipeline is actively filling. **Cost impact**: ~30% more Haiku tokens per quiz in the normal case (13 for a 10-q quiz). On the Haiku 4.5 pricing tier this is sub-cent per quiz ŌĆö worth it for "user gets what they selected". **Exam mode NOT touched** ŌĆö `startExam()` ships all 18 per batch ├Ś 5 = 90 without running through `validateQuestions` (separate known gap; exam has no validation pass). **`injectPBQs` also unaffected** ŌĆö splices 1-for-1 so doesn't change count. **UAT**: 8 new v4.43.4 assertions ŌĆö startQuiz body extractable (sanity), `DROPOUT_BUFFER` uses the exact `Math.max(3, Math.ceil(qCount * 0.3))` formula, initial fetch passes `qCount + DROPOUT_BUFFER`, retry-to-fill block exists, retry passes `deficit + DROPOUT_BUFFER`, retry wraps in try/catch with `retryErr`, **regression guard** on the old `// Acceptable shortfall` comment, **regression guard** on the old `length < Math.ceil(qCount / 2)` branch. All scoped via function-body extraction (`_startQuizBody`) so they don't accidentally match elsewhere. Also updated the 2 existing version-string assertions (4.43.3 ŌåÆ 4.43.4). Total UAT: 2471 ŌåÆ **2479** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.43.4`. |

| v4.43.0 | **Keyword highlighting in question stems** ŌĆö new product feature (minor version bump, not maintenance). CompTIA exam stems use specific trap words that change meaning: *"Which of the following is NOT..."*, *"MOST secure option EXCEPT for..."*, *"The FIRST step in the troubleshooting methodology..."*. Missing these words is the #2 wrong-answer mode after "I didn't know it" ŌĆö test-takers skim and miss the negation or superlative. This release auto-highlights them at render time to train the eye to catch them on the real exam. **14-keyword dictionary**: `NOT`, `EXCEPT`, `CANNOT` (negation), `MOST`, `LEAST`, `BEST`, `WORST`, `PRIMARY` (superlatives), `FIRST`, `LAST`, `NEXT` (sequence), `ALWAYS`, `NEVER`, `ONLY` (absolutes). Deliberately **excludes** `all`, `none`, `any`, `could`, `should`, `would`, `which` ŌĆö those are too common in plain prose, would produce visual noise. UAT regression-guards the exclusion list. **Rendering approach**: new `setQuestionText(el, raw)` helper that does `el.innerHTML = highlightExamKeywords(escHtml(raw))` ŌĆö single entry point for all 5 render paths (quiz stem, exam stem, review page, CLI sim scenario, topology scenario). Escapes HTML first (XSS-safe since `q.question` is AI-generated), then wraps keywords in `<strong class="exam-keyword">`. Word-boundary regex with `gi` flags so case is preserved (lowercase "not" in prose stays lowercase but still styled ŌĆö doesn't visually conflict since the styling is background + color, not text-transform). **CSS**: subtle chip styling ŌĆö bold + accent-light color + 10% accent background + inset bottom-border underline. Light theme gets a slightly darker accent variant for contrast. NOT a big shout ŌĆö keywords should catch the eye without dominating the sentence. **What's NOT touched**: Explain Further content, Topic Deep Dive, Topic Brief, Analytics pages ŌĆö those are teacher-generated content, not questions. Keywords only appear in question stems where the pedagogy win lives. **UAT**: 44 new v4.43.0 assertions ŌĆö constants/helpers present, all 14 keywords covered, 7 ambiguous words explicitly excluded, 5 render paths wired up, 2 regression guards against old `textContent`-based rendering, 3 CSS presence checks, 2 XSS-safety guards (escape before highlight, null-input handling), and a 7-case behavioral smoke test that verifies upper-case / mixed-case / multiple-keywords / plain-prose / word-boundary / excluded-word / escaped-HTML-entity behavior all work correctly. Total UAT: 2368 ŌåÆ **2412** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.43.0`. |

| v4.42.4 | **Readiness algorithm ŌĆö within-domain question-count weighting fix** ŌĆö user asked for a correctness audit of the exam readiness calculator. Audit surfaced one real flaw and three deferrable tuning preferences. Shipped the correctness fix; filed the rest on Board #1 gated on SaaS-pivot user data. **The flaw**: `getReadinessScore()` was computing domain accuracy as the simple average of per-topic percentages (`pctSum / count`), giving equal weight to a topic with 2 questions and one with 200. The real CompTIA exam weights every question equally ŌĆö so a user who is 95% on OSPF (20 weighted Q's) and 50% on BGP (4 weighted Q's) has a real-exam-equivalent implementation accuracy of `(19+2)/(20+4) = 87.5%`, not the simple average of 72.5%. The v4.42.3 catalog expansion (40 ŌåÆ 50 topics) made the flaw more visible because new child topics start with 0 questions while parent umbrellas have many ŌĆö high topic-count variance makes the averaging distortion bigger. **The fix**: ~10 lines in `getReadinessScore()`. Swap `pctSum += pct; count++` aggregation for `wCorrect += topicMap[t].wCorrect; wTotal += topicMap[t].wTotal` ŌĆö then domain average is `wCorrect / wTotal * 100` across all topics in the domain, properly weighted by question count. Unstudied-domain behavior preserved (still computes 0 and drags the score down). The 40/25/20/15 signal weights (accuracy / coverage / recency / volume), 420-870 scaling, domain weights (23/20/19/14/24), difficulty multipliers (Hard 2.0 / Exam 1.5 / Found 1.0), exam-mode boost 1.3├Ś, 7-day recency boost 2├Ś, 14-day recency decay window, and 500-Q volume cap are all **untouched** ŌĆö those were reviewed and deemed correct. **Deferred tuning opportunities** (filed as issue #139, gated on SaaS-pivot user data): (1) Recency denominator is `totalTopics` not `studiedTopics`, which subtly makes recency signal partially a coverage signal, redundant with the Coverage signal itself; (2) No PBQ weighting in accuracy calc ŌĆö real CompTIA exam weights PBQs heavier than MCQs, but the algorithm treats them the same; (3) Triple-penalty for low coverage (coverage ├Ś 0.5 under 5 topics, unstudied domains = 0 accuracy, small recency numerator) ŌĆö mathematically fair but potentially discouraging for early users. Each of these is a judgment call without clear "right" answer for a single-user tool; revisit when SaaS has real user data to observe what correlates with pass rates. **UAT**: 10 new v4.42.4 assertions ŌĆö 5 structural regression guards (new `wCorrect/wTotal` aggregation present, old `pctSum/count` pattern gone, `bucket.wTotal > 0` division-by-zero guard) + 5 behavioral smoke assertions on a synthetic fixture that proves (a) new logic gives 87.5% on unequal-Q-count data, (b) old logic would have given 72.5%, (c) new vs old differ by >10% when Q counts vary, (d) new and old agree when Q counts are equal (shows the fix is a strict upgrade, not a swap), (e) unstudied domain still returns 0. Total UAT: 2260 ŌåÆ **2270** passing. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.42.4`. |
| v4.42.3-audit | **Maintenance pass ŌĆö UAT value-density audit + CLAUDE.md history reorg + module-split issue filed** ŌĆö docs/tests addendum to v4.42.3 (no production code change, no version bump, no redeploy). User flagged growth concern: UAT at 2257 assertions felt unwieldy. Audit findings: suite has fewer outright duplicates than it looked (only 9 CSS-class duplicates, 17 js-include duplicates across 841 checks). Real problem is 240 pure function-name-presence checks (`js.includes('function foo(')`) that prove a string exists without proving the feature works ŌĆö if the function is gone, UAT fails loud but so does everything else downstream, so the assertions add no signal. **Actions taken:** (1) Added a TESTING PHILOSOPHY header to `tests/uat.js` establishing the preference order (behavioral smoke > structural regex > regression guards > dynamic consistency checks > AVOID pure function-name presence AND AVOID hardcoding versions in 3+ places). Sets the norm for future additions. | v4.42.0 | **Animation pass ŌĆö celebration toasts + milestone unlocks + motion hardening** ŌĆö eight fixes shipped together after an audit of the homepage/results animation story flagged real gaps. User scope was explicit: *"do all the fixes today aswell as the 3 you were suggesting to defer. i want them all done for V4.42.0"*. **(1) Readiness score roll-up**: `renderReadinessCard()` used to hot-swap `numEl.textContent = predicted` which wiped the old value instantly. Now reads `parseInt(numEl.textContent, 10)` as the previous value and calls the existing `animateCount('readiness-num', oldVal, predicted, 900)` helper when they differ ŌĆö the 900ms cubic-ease-out count-up makes the score visibly climb (e.g. 612 ŌåÆ 647) after a quiz. Falls back to direct assignment on first render (NaN old value). **(2) Homepage-card refresh hooks in finish() / submitExam()**: pre-v4.42 the setup-page cards (`renderStatsCard`, `renderReadinessCard`) were only refreshed when the user navigated back via `goSetup()` ŌĆö so the next goSetup render showed stale data for a split second before recomputing. Both finish/submitExam now call `renderStatsCard()` and `renderReadinessCard()` directly after `saveToHistory()`, so by the time the user hits Back the DOM already reflects the new history row. **(3) Milestone celebration toast + (4) evaluateMilestones return capture**: discovered a pre-existing architectural bug ŌĆö `evaluateMilestones()` was NEVER called from `finish()` or `submitExam()`, milestones only unlocked lazily when the user happened to open the Analytics page. Big ones like `first_quiz`, `hundred_qs`, `perfect_quiz`, `first_exam`, `exam_pass`, `hardcore_pass`, `streak_7`, `streak_30` would silently accrue in localStorage but never celebrate. Now `evaluateMilestones()` is called at the end of both finish() and submitExam(), the returned `newlyUnlocked` array is captured, and each unlock fires a staggered `showMilestoneCelebration(id)` call (500ms + 900ms per milestone in finish; 900ms base in submitExam so it doesn't collide with the exam-pass confetti). New helpers: `showMilestoneCelebration(id)` reads `MILESTONE_DEFS` to find the icon/label/desc, calls `showCelebrationToast(icon+label, desc)` + `launchMiniConfetti()`. `showCelebrationToast(titleText, subText)` clones the `showErrorToast` DOM-append pattern but with a distinct purple/gold gradient palette and a 3800ms display window. **(5) @media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce) gate**: audit found zero accessibility coverage for motion-sensitive users. Added a global block to styles.css that neutralizes `.celebration-toast` transitions (.01ms linear), kills `.streak-pulse` animations (`animation: none`), strips transform transitions from `.tf-chip`, and reduces `.dg-ring-fill` + `.grade-fill` stroke-dashoffset transitions to .01ms so the final state is still painted without visible motion. **(6) Streak pulse on increment**: new module-level `_pendingStreakPulse` flag set in finish/submitExam when `getStreak().current > _prevStreakBefore` (snapshot captured before `updateStreak()`). `renderStreakBadge()` consumes the flag in `goSetup()`, adds a `.streak-pulse` class that triggers a 900ms `@keyframes streakPulse` (scale 1ŌåÆ1.12ŌåÆ1 with an orange `box-shadow: 0 0 0 10px rgba(251,146,60,0)` ripple), and cleans up via `animationend`. Flag is set while the setup page is hidden (during results) and consumed when setup becomes visible, so the user sees the pulse *on arrival* at the homepage, not during the quiz. **(7) Weak Spots FLIP rerank animation**: `renderTodaysFocus()` now uses First-Last-Invert-Play. Captures `getBoundingClientRect()` of each existing `.tf-chip[data-topic]` into an `oldRects` map BEFORE the innerHTML rewrite, stamps `data-topic` on new chips so lookup keys match, then iterates the new chips post-rewrite: for each one that existed before, computes `dx/dy` deltas between old and new positions, applies `translate(dx,dy)` + `transition: none`, forces a reflow via `void el.offsetWidth`, then releases by setting `transition: transform 420ms cubic-bezier(0.2, 0.8, 0.2, 1)` and clearing the transform. Chip appears to glide from old slot to new. **Critical supporting change**: finish() and submitExam() no longer call `renderTodaysFocus()` directly (the v4.38.7 defensive calls). The double-render was defeating FLIP ŌĆö first call happened while `#page-setup` was hidden (all bounding rects 0), second call measured the already-updated DOM with no diff detected. Moving the single call to `goSetup()` alone gives FLIP a real old ŌåÆ new delta to animate. UAT has regression guards (`finish() no longer calls renderTodaysFocus (FLIP guard)`) so a future refactor can't silently reintroduce the double-render. **(8) Mini confetti variant**: `launchMiniConfetti()` is a subtler cousin of `launchConfetti()` ŌĆö 40 particles (vs 150), 80 frames (vs 200), 5-color gold/accent palette (`#fbbf24`, `#f59e0b`, `#fde047`, `#7c6ff7`, `#22c55e`) vs the 8-color rainbow, origin point at `(canvas.width/2, 80)` (near the top where the celebration toast lives) vs randomized across the screen, radial emission pattern (angle = `2ŽĆ * i / count + jitter`) vs falling-from-top. Subtler celebration for milestone unlocks without stealing thunder from the big exam-pass burst. **UAT**: 42 new v4.42.0 assertions verify every piece ŌĆö readiness roll-up wiring, celebration toast DOM lifecycle, `showMilestoneCelebration` reading `MILESTONE_DEFS`, evaluateMilestones return capture in both finish and submitExam, FLIP rerank (data-topic stamping, `oldRects` capture, inverse transform application, transitionend cleanup), streak-pulse flag lifecycle (declared, set in finish/submitExam, consumed in renderStreakBadge, CSS `@keyframes streakPulse`), mini-confetti particle count + palette separation, `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)` block presence, and FLIP guards preventing future regressions of the finish/submitExam ŌåÆ renderTodaysFocus double-render. Total UAT: 2126 ŌåÆ **2168** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.42.0`. |
