| v4.39.0 | **Topology Builder ŌĆö bigger canvas + force-directed auto-layout for AI-generated topologies** ŌĆö user posted a screenshot of a "standard school network" generated via the topology builder's AI Generate, devices were all bunched in the upper-left quadrant of the canvas: *"the network as you can see it totally bunched together which is not very appealing. i need the topolgiies generated to be perfectly spaced out across the canvas. If we need the canvas to be bigger by all means i dont mind."* Two-part fix. (1) **Canvas bumped 1400├Ś820 ŌåÆ 1800├Ś1100** (~72% more area). `TB_CANVAS_W`/`TB_CANVAS_H` constants updated, SVG `viewBox` in `index.html` updated, and `.tb-workspace` / `.tb-canvas-wrap` / `.tb-canvas` `min-height` raised from 720px ŌåÆ 900px to match the taller aspect ratio. All existing bounds clamps in `tbClientToSvg` and `tbOnMouseMove` already referenced the constants so they updated automatically. (2) **New `tbAutoLayout(state)` force-directed function** ŌĆö runs unconditionally inside `tbDeepValidateAndFix` after AI generation, replacing the old "stacked-at-(400,400)" detector that only caught devices stuck at exact defaults and missed Haiku's gently-bunched output. Algorithm: detects clustered seeds (max-min spread < 250px on either axis) and grid-seeds them across the canvas first, then runs 260 iterations of a force-directed simulation with pair-wise repulsion (`REPULSE = 9000 / dist┬▓`), cable-based spring attraction (`SPRING = 0.06`, `IDEAL_LINK = 200`), velocity damping (0.85), velocity cap (30), and bounds clamping with 100├Ś90 padding. Final hard-separation pass (up to 30 iterations) guarantees no two devices closer than `MIN_SEP = 150` regardless of what the simulation converged to. Returns count of devices that moved more than 8px so `tbDeepValidateAndFix` can append "Auto-layout repositioned N device(s) for clarity" to the user-facing fix list. (3) **AI prompt updated** to mention the new 1800├Ś1100 canvas, the 150-1650 / 120-980 spread range, and the 180px minimum spacing rule ŌĆö with a note that positions get auto-relayouted post-generation, so if Haiku ignores the instruction (which it often does), the deterministic post-pass still fixes it. (4) **9 new UAT assertions** covering function presence, constant + parameter wiring, the `tbDeepValidateAndFix` call site, the AI-prompt updates, and a behavioral smoke test that extracts `tbAutoLayout` into a Function() sandbox, feeds it 8 devices stacked at (400,400) ┬▒5px, and asserts the post-layout min pair distance is Ōēź140px. Live-preview verification: `tbAutoLayout` was fed a 10-device topology mimicking the user's screenshot (firewall ŌåÆ IDS ŌåÆ router ŌåÆ LB ŌåÆ switch ŌåÆ 3 PCs + 2 servers + printer, all clustered around 500,470), and the function spread them across x:455ŌĆō1700, y:90ŌĆō859 with min pair distance 195px. Total UAT: 2059 ŌåÆ **2069** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.39.0`. |
| v4.38.7 | **Weak Spots v2 ŌĆö robust, real-time ranking algorithm** ŌĆö user posted a screenshot of the front-page "­¤Ä» Weak spots" chip row and asked for "a more robust and deeper calculation algorithm for what my weak spots are and they need to update in real time." The old `getTodaysFocusTopics()` was a 15-line heuristic: +2 per wrong-bank entry + a flat `(0.75 - accuracy) * 20` bonus for topics under 75% history accuracy. Eight weaknesses: no recency decay (a 3-month-old wrong counted the same as a 1-hour-old wrong), no confidence interval (one bad 5-Q run instantly dominated), no difficulty weighting, no domain importance, no staleness for topics you studied once and forgot, no hooks into quiz-completion paths for real-time updates, and it lumped untouched topics (no signal) in with weak topics (bad signal). Rewrote as `computeWeakSpotScores()` ŌĆö a proper scoring model that combines four signals: (1) **recency-decayed wrong-bank count** ŌĆö exponential decay with 7-day half-life (`WEAK_HALF_LIFE_WRONGS_MS = 7 * 86400000`), difficulty-weighted via the existing `diffWeight()` helper (Hard 2.0├Ś / Exam 1.5├Ś / Foundational 1.0├Ś), half-credit for entries where `rightCount >= 1` since they're already partially graduated. A wrong from yesterday counts ~0.9, a wrong from 14 days ago counts ~0.25, a wrong from 60 days ago counts ~0.003 ŌĆö old mistakes fade. (2) **Bayesian posterior accuracy gap** ŌĆö recency-decayed weighted correct/total from `loadHistory()` (14-day half-life via `WEAK_HALF_LIFE_HIST_MS`, exam-mode boost 1.3├Ś, difficulty-weighted). Raw accuracy is smoothed with a Beta(2,2) prior: `posterior = (wCorrect + 2) / (wTotal + 4)`. This means a single bad 3/5 run doesn't instantly flag the topic as weak ŌĆö the prior acts like 2 phantom correct + 2 phantom wrong answers, so the posterior only moves meaningfully once you've built real volume. Gap = `max(0, 0.85 - posterior)` against the `WEAK_TARGET_ACC = 0.85` mastery threshold. (3) **Staleness bonus** ŌĆö topics untouched for more than `WEAK_STALENESS_DAYS = 14` days start accruing up to a `WEAK_STALENESS_CAP = 2.0` multiplier, so a topic you once mastered but haven't revisited in 6 weeks doesn't fade off the radar entirely. Computed as `(daysSince - 14) / 14`, capped. (4) **Domain importance multiplier** ŌĆö `_weakDomainMultiplier(topic)` reads `TOPIC_DOMAINS[topic]` and returns `DOMAIN_WEIGHTS[dom] / 0.2` (average of the 5 weights), so a weak Troubleshooting topic (24%) outranks a weak Security topic (14%) at equal raw badness ŌĆö matches the real N10-009 domain distribution. Range is ~0.7├Ś (security) to ~1.2├Ś (troubleshooting). Final score = `(wrongsRecent * 3.0 + accGap * 25.0 + staleness * 2.0) * domainMul`. **Low-signal filter**: topics with `wTotal < 1 && wrongsRecent < 0.5` are excluded ŌĆö that's "untouched, not weak" (the Study Plan card handles coverage). **Backward compat**: `getTodaysFocusTopics(limit)` is now a 1-line wrapper around `computeWeakSpotScores().slice(0, limit).map(r => r.topic)` so the existing callers (Focused preset on the setup page, weakest-topic fallback in `applyPreset`) still work unchanged. **Real-time hooks**: `renderTodaysFocus()` now shows a tooltip per chip with the computed posterior accuracy, recent-wrongs count, and staleness-in-days ŌĆö so you can hover/tap a chip and see *why* it's flagged. Added `renderTodaysFocus()` calls directly into `finish()` and `submitExam()` after the `saveToHistory()` line, so every quiz and exam completion refreshes the chips immediately (goSetup already called it on back-navigation; these new calls cover direct page-switch paths). **27 new UAT assertions** verify every piece: constant definitions (`WEAK_HALF_LIFE_*`, `WEAK_TARGET_ACC`, `WEAK_STALENESS_*`), helper definitions (`_weakDecay`, `_weakDomainMultiplier`), the Bayesian prior regex (`(wCorrect + 2) / (wTotal + 4)`), `diffWeight`/`_weakDomainMultiplier`/exam-boost usage inside the function body, descending sort, low-signal exclusion guard, graduation half-credit logic, the `finish()` + `submitExam()` refresh hooks, and `renderTodaysFocus()` displaying the posterior in its tooltip. One assertion is a **behavioral smoke test**: extracts `computeWeakSpotScores` + `_weakDecay` + `_weakDomainMultiplier` + the constants into a sandbox, stubs `loadWrongBank`/`loadHistory`/`TOPIC_DOMAINS`/`DOMAIN_WEIGHTS`/`diffWeight`/`MIXED_TOPIC`/`EXAM_TOPIC`, runs the function against a synthetic fixture (3 recent wrongs on Troubleshooting + 1 recent wrong + moderate history on PKI + IPv6 history + a Mixed noise entry), and asserts: (a) non-empty results, (b) Mixed topic is excluded, (c) untouched-topic sentinel is excluded, (d) rows are sorted descending, (e) heavy-wrong Troubleshooting outranks lighter PKI, (f) Bayesian posterior is computed and in (0,1) for topics with history, (g) `wrongsRaw` display count is correct. Offline tests can't exercise real user behavior, but they CAN prove the algorithm produces the right ranking for the exact class of input the user's real wrong-bank will have. Total UAT: 2028 ŌåÆ **2059** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.38.7`. |
| v4.38.6 | **Auto-negotiation vs Auto-MDIX ground truth ŌĆö Ethernet physical layer hardening** ŌĆö user hit a Haiku-generated Cabling & Topology MCQ whose stem asked about automatic MDI/MDIX pin detection on a too-long cable run but marked "Auto-negotiation, which automatically detects cable polarity and adjusts pin assignments" as the correct answer. This is a conflation: auto-negotiation (IEEE 802.3u clause 28) handles SPEED and DUPLEX only; Auto-MDIX (IEEE 802.3ab clause 40) is the distinct feature that detects MDI/MDIX pinout and swaps TX/RX. The two are bundled on modern gear which is why Haiku generates it wrong and Sonnet validation missed it ŌĆö the v4.38.5 ground-truth tables (`GT_PORTS`, `GT_OSI`, `GT_WIFI_*`) had no Ethernet-physical-layer coverage. Belt-and-braces fix in two layers so the class of bug can't resurface: (1) **`GT_ETHERNET` truth table** ŌĆö 6 entries covering auto-negotiation, auto-MDIX, MDI/MDIX, straight-through vs crossover, duplex mismatch, and PoE standards (802.3af/at/bt 15.4/30/60/100W). Each entry is a (feature, authoritative description) pair. Source comments cite the specific 802.3 clause so future refactors can't erode the facts. (2) **`_buildGtHint()` Ethernet branch** ŌĆö new `ethRe` regex fires on any of `auto-negotiat`, `auto-mdix`, `mdix`, `mdi/mdix`, `crossover`, `straight-through`, `duplex`, `poe`, `poe+`, or any `802.3x` reference in the question text or topic name. When it matches, the helper unconditionally prepends both the auto-negotiation AND auto-MDIX facts to the AUTHORITATIVE FACTS block (surfacing the distinction even if only one is named in the stem), plus conditional duplex-mismatch and PoE-wattage facts on keyword match. This means every Tier A teacher call site (`explainFurther`, `showTopicDeepDive`, `fetchTopicBrief`) that gets an Ethernet-physical question now sees the two features spelled out as distinct before the Sonnet teacher model writes a word ŌĆö no more conflation in deep dives, topic guides, or pre-quiz briefs. (3) **`_groundTruthOk()` programmatic guard** ŌĆö new `mdiStemRe` detects question stems asking about MDI/MDIX, pin assignments, crossover, or straight-through cable auto-detection. If a stem matches AND the marked answer invokes auto-negotiation without also mentioning auto-MDIX, `_groundTruthOk()` returns false and `validateQuestions()` drops the question cold before it reaches the quiz UI. Reverse check with `speedDuplexStemRe`: if the stem is clearly about speed/duplex negotiation and the marked answer blames auto-MDIX, that's the inverse conflation ŌĆö also dropped. This is the authoritative guard ŌĆö even if the teacher prompt's GT injection somehow fails or gets bypassed, the programmatic validator in the quiz generation pipeline still catches the question. The user's exact bug (MDI/MDIX stem ŌåÆ auto-negotiation answer) now fails both layers. (4) **12 new UAT assertions** verify the constant exists, the regex is wired, both features are unconditionally surfaced on ethernet-keyword match, the AUTHORITATIVE FACTS header is emitted, and the `_groundTruthOk` guards are present. One assertion is a behavioral smoke test: it extracts `GT_ETHERNET` + `_buildGtHint` into a sandbox via `Function()`, calls the helper with a Cabling & Topology style MDI/MDIX stem, and asserts the returned string includes both "SPEED and DUPLEX only" and "pin assignments" ŌĆö offline tests can't exercise real Claude output, but they CAN prove the helper emits the right facts for the exact scenario that broke. Total UAT: 2016 ŌåÆ **2028** passing. Validation-audit regression gate still green (62.5% catch rate, 0 false positives). Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.38.6`. |
| v4.38.5 | **AI teacher pipeline audit ŌĆö Tier A/B/C hardening** ŌĆö after v4.38.4 closed the quiz-question validation loop, a deeper audit surfaced 7 other Claude call sites that render content the user trusts as authoritative (explanations, topic guides, coach responses). Every one of them was still on Haiku 4.5 (same model that slipped 6/16 broken questions pre-fix) with no ground-truth checks and no caching. This release hardens all 7. (1) **New `CLAUDE_TEACHER_MODEL = 'claude-sonnet-4-6'` constant** separate from `CLAUDE_MODEL` (Haiku, generation) and `CLAUDE_VALIDATOR_MODEL` (Sonnet, validation). Three-way model split makes intent explicit. (2) **Tier A ŌĆö authoritative study content (3 sites)**: `explainFurther()` (6-section deep dive shown after answer), `showTopicDeepDive()` / `buildTopicDivePrompt()` (full topic guide page), and `fetchTopicBrief()` (pre-quiz topic brief) all swapped to Sonnet. Each now (a) prepends authoritative ground-truth facts via the new `_buildGtHint(text, topicName)` helper which scans the question/topic for protocol keywords and returns a compact "AUTHORITATIVE FACTS" block covering any relevant ports from `GT_PORTS`, OSI layers from `GT_OSI`, and WEP/WPA deprecation warnings; and (b) caches responses via the new shared `_aiCacheGet('namespace', key)` / `_aiCacheSet(...)` helpers backed by `STORAGE.AI_CACHE` (djb2 hash keying + 20-entry LRU trim by access timestamp). Re-opening the same deep dive or topic guide is now a free localStorage hit. (3) **Tier B ŌĆö math must be exact (2 sites)**: `stAskCoach()` (subnet trainer explain-my-mistake) now computes the deterministic binary breakdown (IP / mask / IP-AND-mask network address) from the question's IP+CIDR and stuffs it into the prompt as "AUTHORITATIVE FACTS" before asking Sonnet for an explanation ŌĆö the AI can't hallucinate the math when the answer is staring at it in the prompt. `ptAskCoach()` (port drill explain) now tags the correct `proto ŌåÆ port` as an "AUTHORITATIVE FACT (do not contradict)" line and swaps to Sonnet. (4) **Tier C ŌĆö topology builder coaches (2 sites)**: `tbCoachTopology()` (student topology walkthrough) and `tbExplainDevice()` (single-device role explanation) both swapped to Sonnet. `tbGenerateAiTopology()` deliberately stays on Haiku because it's bulk JSON generation that already has `tbDeepValidateAndFix` as a post-pass ŌĆö a Sonnet upgrade there would triple costs for minimal quality gain. `fetchQuestions()` also stays on Haiku for the same reason (validated by the Sonnet validator second pass). (5) **23 new UAT structural assertions** verify the constants exist and point to Sonnet, helpers are defined, every Tier A/B/C call site references `CLAUDE_TEACHER_MODEL`, Tier A sites use `_buildGtHint` and `_aiCacheGet/Set` with the correct namespace, Tier B sites embed the "AUTHORITATIVE FACTS" block, and generation paths (`fetchQuestions`, `tbGenerateAiTopology`) still use `CLAUDE_MODEL` for cost. A helper `_fnBody(src, name)` walks brace depth to extract individual function bodies so the assertions scope to the right call site. Offline tests can't exercise AI output, but they CAN prove the hardening is wired ŌĆö a refactor that silently reverts any of these fixes will now fail UAT. Total UAT: 1993 ŌåÆ **2016** passing. The validation-audit regression gate still runs in UAT; programmatic catch rate holds at 62.5% with 0 false positives. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.38.5`. |
| v4.38.4 | **Question quality pipeline ŌĆö deep audit + 5-fix upgrade** ŌĆö after a user hit an explanation-answer mismatch bug (DC three-tier question: explanation correctly described "access tier contains servers and storage" but answer was marked as Core), ran a deep vulnerability audit of the 3-layer quality pipeline (generation prompt ŌåÆ AI validation pass ŌåÆ programmatic `validateQuestions`). Built `tests/validation-audit.js` ŌĆö a 20-question broken-corpus regression fixture covering 16 distinct failure modes (premise-answer contradiction, explanation-answer mismatch, wrong port numbers, two valid answers, no correct answer, keyword overlap, WPA3 contradiction, short-option keyword blindness, outdated fact, stub explanation, subnet math error, missing/invalid objective, malformed answer letter, explicit wrong-letter claim, subjective qualifier GOOD, negation phrasing GOOD) plus 4 clean controls. Baseline v4.38.3 catch rate was **31.3% (5/16)**. Shipped 5 fixes: (1) **Unique-word scoring with negation guard** ŌĆö `validateQuestions()` mcq branch now tokenizes each option minus stopwords, computes the distinctive token set per option via set subtraction, and scores each set against the explanation with a 40-char-before + 30-char-after negation-context window. If any distractor scores Ōēź1 AND beats the marked answer's score, the question is dropped. Only runs for non-negation questions (skips on NOT/EXCEPT/"which not"). (2) **Ground truth tables** ŌĆö new `GT_PORTS` (27 protocolŌåÆport mappings), `GT_OSI` (30 protocolŌåÆlayer), `GT_WIFI_BROKEN` (`['wep']`), `GT_WIFI_DEPRECATED` (`['wpa']`) static tables. `_groundTruthOk(q)` checks port-for-protocol questions, protocol-for-port questions, OSI layer questions, and wireless security questions against the tables ŌĆö any deterministic N10-009 fact with a wrong answer gets rejected cold. (3) **Numeric-option path** ŌĆö `_numericOptionOk(q)` detects questions where all 4 options are numeric (subnet math, port numbers, host counts) and scans the explanation for final-answer phrases (`leaves N`, `N usable`, `= N`, `total of N`, `results in N`) ŌĆö if the phrase value doesn't match the marked answer's numeric value, the question is dropped. (4) **CI regression gate** ŌĆö `tests/validation-audit.js` now enforces a `MIN_CATCH_RATE = 60` floor and `MAX_FP_RATE = 0` ceiling, exiting non-zero on breach. `tests/uat.js` spawns it via `execSync` as a new "Validation audit: regression gate" test, so a refactor to `validateQuestions()` can never silently regress below the known baseline and the UAT suite will fail loudly. (5) **Sonnet AI validator** ŌĆö new `CLAUDE_VALIDATOR_MODEL = 'claude-sonnet-4-6'` constant alongside the existing Haiku `CLAUDE_MODEL`. `aiValidateQuestions()` now fires its second-pass semantic check against Sonnet instead of Haiku, because the remaining slips after fixes 1-3 are all deeper reasoning failures (premise-answer logical contradictions, "no correct answer" questions, two-valid-answer questions) that Haiku can't reliably catch. Generation stays on Haiku for cost/latency; validation trades a few cents per quiz for dramatically better semantic judgment. Post-fix programmatic-only catch rate: **62.5% (10/16)** with 0 false positives (up from 31.3%). Sonnet validator expected to catch most of the remaining 6 semantic slips in production. New fixes caught in audit: SSH port wrong, HTTPS port wrong, WEP outdated, access-list keyword overlap, subnet math 6 vs 8. 1 new UAT assertion (1993 total). Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.38.4`. |

Long-function count: **11 ŌåÆ 8** (under tightened threshold of 8). Remaining offenders for a future refactor session: `fetchQuestions` (120), `submitExam` (117), `evaluateMilestones` (89), `renderCliSim` (92), `renderTopology` (131), `aiValidateQuestions` (86), `explainFurther` (101), and the elephant `renderAnalytics` (482). **Tech debt #17 fixed**: bulk-replaced inline `.style.*` assignments with CSS utility classes ŌĆö `.is-hidden { display: none !important; }` and `.is-dimmed { opacity: 0.5 }`. All 74 `style.display = 'none'/'block'/'flex'/''` toggles became `classList.add/remove/toggle('is-hidden', ...)`, all 7 `style.opacity = '0.5'/'1'` toggles became `classList.toggle('is-dimmed', ...)`. Inline `.style.*` count: **117 ŌåÆ 37** (-80). Tech-debt monitor threshold tightened from 105 to 50 to lock in the win. **Important follow-up**: 17 elements in `index.html` had `style="display:none"` baked into the markup; a `classList.remove('is-hidden')` from JS could not override that inline style, so Playwright tests waiting on `subnet-next-btn`, `port-game`, `weak-banner`, `stats-card`, etc. all failed. All 17 inline `display:none` HTML attributes were converted to `class="... is-hidden"` so JS toggling actually shows the elements. Lesson: when you migrate JS toggling to a CSS class, audit the matching HTML markup for inline styles that would shadow the class. **Tech debt #23 fixed**: dead code sweep ŌĆö removed unreferenced `ipToArr()` helper (replaced long ago by `octetsFromIp()`-style usage) and the unused `N10_009_OBJECTIVE_RE` constant (the actual objective validation in `validateQuestions` uses an inline substring regex with capture group for "Obj 1.4" / "1.4 ŌĆö Routing" extraction, so the anchored constant was a duplicate that drifted out of use). UAT swapped the `N10_009_OBJECTIVE_RE` symbol assertion for a regex-pattern presence check. **Tech debt #20 fixed**: service worker now hard-caps the runtime cache at `CACHE_MAX_ENTRIES = 60` and FIFO-evicts via a new `trimCache()` helper called after every `cache.put`. 5xx responses are no longer cached and now fall back to the cached copy when available, so a Vercel/origin outage no longer breaks the offline app. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.11.8`. **Tech debt #24 fixed**: new `.github/workflows/auto-add-to-board.yml` listens for `issues.opened/labeled/reopened` and adds the issue to Board #1 (`tech-debt`/`bug`) or Board #2 (`feature-idea`) via GraphQL `addProjectV2ItemById`. Replaces the unreliable built-in GitHub Projects auto-add workflow that did not fire for REST-API-created issues. Project IDs are looked up at runtime by project number so they're never hardcoded. Both this workflow and the existing tech-debt issue-creation block in `ci.yml` now use `secrets.PROJECT_TOKEN || secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN` ŌĆö `PROJECT_TOKEN` is a PAT with the `project` scope (the default `GITHUB_TOKEN` lacks it, which is why the existing inline GraphQL block in the tech-debt job had been silently failing) |

| v4.31.1 | **Fix quiz question count bug** ŌĆö Quiz sometimes generated 1 or 6 questions instead of the requested 5. | v4.28.1 | **AI Generation Reliability Fix** ŌĆö fixes "invalid topology" error when generating complex scenarios like "2 data centres connected via VPN". Root causes: (1) `max_tokens` was 4096 ŌĆö complex topologies with VPN configs routinely exceeded this, causing truncated JSON that the parser couldn't handle. Bumped to 8192. (2) No retry mechanism ŌĆö a single parse failure immediately showed an error. Now uses a two-attempt strategy: first attempt with full prompt, second attempt with a simplified focused prompt if the first fails. (3) Parser couldn't handle truncated JSON ŌĆö added Stage 5 truncation repair that counts open/close braces/brackets and attempts to close them to salvage partial results. (4) Semantic expansion was too verbose ŌĆö "data centres" expanded into a paragraph-long description that overwhelmed Haiku. Shortened all 16 expansions to concise device-type references. (5) "Output ONLY valid JSON" rule was buried at the end of the prompt (Rule 12) ŌĆö moved to the very first line of the base prompt so the AI sees it before the lengthy device guide. (6) No debugging ŌĆö added `console.log` for raw AI response text, stop_reason, and response length so truncation and parse failures are diagnosable in the browser console. New `_tbCallAiAndParse()` helper encapsulates the fetch+parse+logging cycle. 10 new UAT assertions (1091 total). Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.28.1`. |

| v4.23.1 | **Hotfix: double-click device to open config panel** ŌĆö root cause: `tbOnDeviceMouseDown` called `e.preventDefault()` which suppresses the browser's native `dblclick` event, AND `tbRenderCanvas()` destroys/recreates all device DOM nodes after every mousedown, so the second click of a double-click lands on a freshly created element that never saw the first click. Fix: replaced the unreliable native `dblclick` listener (`tbAttachDoubleClick`) with a manual timestamp-based double-click detector inside `tbOnDeviceMouseDown` ŌĆö tracks `tbLastClickDevId` + `tbLastClickTime`, fires `tbOpenConfigPanel(id)` if same device clicked within 400ms. | v4.21.0 | **Topology Builder Tier 3 ŌĆö AI Coach (closes the TB 3-tier plan)** ŌĆö ships the last tier on the original Topology Builder roadmap: an instructor-style AI walkthrough of whatever the user just built. Complements the Tier 2 static rules engine ŌĆö grader for "is this design broken?", coach for "teach me *why* this design is good and how it maps to the exam." Tier 1+2+3 all now live in a single session today. (1) **Topology serializer** ŌĆö new `tbSerializeTopology(state)` walks the device graph and emits a compact text description the LLM reads well: devices are grouped by type and assigned stable labels (e.g. `Firewall #1`, `Firewall #2` when duplicates exist), then two sections are emitted ŌĆö `INVENTORY:` (one line per device type with counts) and `CONNECTIONS:` (one line per device listing neighbors with their cable type inline, e.g. `- Router ŌåÆ Firewall #1 (Fiber), Switch (Cat6)`). Orphan devices render as `(not connected)` so the coach can call them out. This shape avoids dumping raw JSON at the model, which tends to get LLMs to produce shallow observations. (2) **Response caching** ŌĆö new `tbTopologyHash(state, scenarioId)` produces a deterministic short hash (djb2-style) over a simplified payload: scenario id + device types/positions (rounded to a 20px grid so micro-drags don't bust the cache) + sorted cable endpoints/types. Hash is used as a key in `STORAGE.TB_COACH_CACHE` (new `nplus_tb_coach_cache` localStorage entry). Responses are cached with a timestamp; `tbSaveCoachCache` trims to the 10 most recent entries. Cache hit ŌåÆ modal renders instantly with a `cached` pill next to the scenario title, no API call. This means re-opening a modal you just closed is free, and iterating a topology only bills for the meaningful changes. (3) **Coach entry point** ŌĆö new async `tbCoachTopology()` (a) short-circuits on empty canvas with a toast, (b) short-circuits with a toast pointing to Settings if `STORAGE.KEY` is empty (no API call attempted), (c) checks cache and early-returns on hit, (d) shows the modal in loading state via `tbShowCoachModalLoading(scenario)` which renders a spinning ring + "Coach is analyzing your topologyŌĆ” (usually 3-5 seconds)" sub-line, (e) calls `CLAUDE_API_URL` with `CLAUDE_MODEL` (haiku 4.5), `max_tokens: 1500`, and a prompt that sets the instructor persona, feeds the scenario context + serialized topology, and asks for a strict JSON response with six keys: `tour` (2-3 sentence walkthrough), `strengths[]` (2-4 wins tied to objectives), `concerns[]` (2-4 things the static grader might miss), `upgrades[]` (2-3 actionable upgrades with rationale), `objectives[]` (2-4 N10-009 objectives exercised), `studyTip` (1 sentence pointing to what to drill next). Response is cleaned of any stray markdown fences (`\u0060\u0060\u0060json ... \u0060\u0060\u0060`), parsed with a JSON.parse + fallback `{...}` regex extract so the modal still works if the model wraps its output. Cached + rendered on success, `tbShowCoachModalError(msg)` on any failure path with a Retry button that just re-invokes `tbCoachTopology()`. (4) **Coach modal** ŌĆö new `#tb-coach-modal` shares the overlay/card/backdrop styling from Tier 2's grade modal (class-reuse: `.tb-grade-modal`) but with a sky-blue accent palette distinct from the purple grader. Structure: coach head (cyan gradient band with scenario title + tour paragraph) ŌåÆ 4 severity-colored sections (Strengths green, Concerns amber, Upgrades sky, Objectives purple) each with bullet lists ŌåÆ final "Study next" callout in a dashed purple border box. New CSS block (~140 lines) covering `.tb-coach-loading`, `.tb-coach-spinner` (4px ring with top-color accent + `tb-coach-spin` keyframe), `.tb-coach-error`, `.tb-coach-head`, `.tb-coach-cached` (pill badge), `.tb-coach-section` + 4 section variants, `.tb-coach-list`, `.tb-coach-tip`, `.tb-tool-btn-coach` (sky-blue gradient toolbar button mirroring the purple `.tb-tool-btn-primary` from Tier 2). Intro banner copy updated to drop the "Tier 3 adds an AI coach" promise since it's now live. 35 new UAT assertions covering the serializer output sections, all 7 new functions, cache trim behavior, API call shape, error handling, HTML wiring, and CSS presence. | v4.20.0 | **Topology Builder Tier 2 ŌĆö Auto-Grader + Scenario Mode + PNG Export** ŌĆö closes the original Tier 2 scope (design validation) from the TB parent plan. Three features shipped together. (1) **Rules engine**: new `TB_GRADE_RULES` array of 12 rules (id/severity/label/hint/test), each `test(state)` inspecting `tbState.devices` + `tbState.cables` via three new graph helpers ŌĆö `tbNeighborsOf(state, id)` returns the device objects on the other end of every cable touching `id`, `tbIsConnectedTo(state, id, type)` checks for a one-hop neighbor of a given type, `tbDevicesOfType(state, type)` filters the device list. Rules: `min-devices` (3+), `no-orphans`, `has-firewall` (critical), `cloud-behind-firewall` (critical ŌĆö every cloud node must touch a firewall), `dmz-exists-if-public` (critical), `public-on-dmz` (critical ŌĆö every public-* device must neighbor a dmz-switch and NOT a regular switch), `dmz-behind-firewall` (critical), `internal-behind-firewall` (warning ŌĆö internal switch must touch a firewall or router), `wlc-wired-to-wap` (warning ŌĆö does a 2-hop WLCŌåÆswitchŌåÆWAP search so WLC/AP/switch triangle passes), `lb-fronts-servers` (warning ŌĆö LB must neighbor 2+ servers or public-*), `ids-positioned` (info), `endpoints-on-internal` (warning ŌĆö PC/printer/voip/iot must not touch dmz-switch). Severity-weighted deductions: critical -20, warning -10, info -5, floor at 0. Letter grade map: A (93+) / A- (87+) / B+ (80+) / B (73+) / C+ (65+) / C (58+) / D (50+) / F. `tbGradeTopology()` entry point runs the scenario-selected rule subset, appends synthetic critical rules for scenario device-count requirements, and calls `tbShowGradeModal()` which renders a fixed-overlay modal (`#tb-grade-modal`) with a score circle (color flips green/yellow/red at 87/70), pill counts (passed/critical/warnings/info), and 4 stacked sections (Critical / Warnings / Suggestions / Passed) each showing rule label + actionable hint. `tbCloseGradeModal()` closes the overlay; backdrop click also closes. Each scenario has `ruleIds` (which rules to run), `requires` (device-count hard requirements ŌĆö `type: 'public-*'` wildcard matches any public-web/file/cloud), `requirements` (string list for display). New `tbSelectedScenario` state (defaults `'free'`). New `tbSetScenario(id)` updates state and calls `tbRenderScenarioPanel()` which populates `#tb-scenario-panel` with the scenario title, description, and requirements `<ul>` ŌĆö hidden entirely in Free Build, shown above the canvas otherwise. Scenario device-count failures appear as critical rule rows labeled "Scenario requires N+ X (you have M)". New `<select id="tb-scenario-select">` in the toolbar wired to `tbSetScenario()`. `openTopologyBuilder()` now calls `tbRenderScenarioPanel()` on open so the panel restores with the current scenario. (3) **PNG export**: new `tbExportPNG()` clones the live `#tb-canvas` SVG, stamps explicit width/height attrs, prepends a dark `#0b1020` `<rect>` background (since the grid pattern is transparent), serializes with `XMLSerializer().serializeToString()`, base64-encodes via `btoa(unescape(encodeURIComponent(...)))` to survive multi-byte chars, feeds it through an `<img>` ŌåÆ `<canvas>` ŌåÆ `canvas.toBlob()` pipeline, and triggers a hidden `<a download>` click. Filename is `{topology_name_sanitized}_{timestamp}.png`. Zero external deps, pure browser APIs. New **­¤Äō Grade** primary button (`.tb-tool-btn-primary` gradient) and **­¤ōĘ Export PNG** ghost button added to the toolbar. Intro banner copy updated to document the new Grade + Export capabilities. New CSS block (~170 lines) for `.tb-grade-modal` + `.tb-grade-backdrop` + `.tb-grade-card` + `.tb-grade-hero` + `.tb-grade-circle` + `.tb-grade-counts` + `.tb-grade-section` (severity-colored left borders for crit/warn/info/pass) + `.tb-scenario-panel` + `.tb-scenario-reqs` + `.tb-tool-btn-primary`. 44 new UAT assertions covering every rule id, every scenario id, all 3 new functions, HTML wiring, and CSS presence. Total UAT: 736 ŌåÆ 780. Cache bumped to `netplus-v4.20.0`. |

| v4.18 | **Topology Builder Tier 1 ŌĆö SVG canvas + device palette + cables + save/load (#74)** ŌĆö first of 3 planned tiers for the visual network topology builder feature (parent #73, Tier 2 = config panels #75, Tier 3 = AI coach #76). New top-level `­¤ö¦ Topology Builder` menu button on the setup page launches a new `#page-topology-builder` with a 1200x700 SVG canvas (grid pattern background) and a left-side device palette containing 7 device types: Router, Switch, WAP, PC, Server, Firewall, Cloud. Each device type is defined in a single `TB_DEVICE_TYPES` map with `label`, `icon`, `color`, `short` ŌĆö adding a new type is one entry. State is a single `tbState` object: `{ id, name, devices: [{id, type, x, y}], cables: [{id, from, to}], created, updated }`, single source of truth, all rendering derives from it. Interactions: **drag from palette** (HTML5 drag API) drops device at cursor position (coordinates translated from client space to SVG viewBox via `createSVGPoint` + `getScreenCTM`); **click device A ŌåÆ click device B** draws a cable (second click completes, clicking the same device cancels); **drag a placed device** moves it within canvas bounds (50/40 padding enforced); **click empty canvas** deselects; **Delete/Backspace** removes selected device (cascade removes any cables touching it) or selected cable; **Escape** cancels current selection and pending cable. Guardrails: **15-device cap** (toast when full), **self-loop prevention**, **duplicate cable detection** (either direction), **device cap enforced before add**, **input field detection** so Delete inside an input doesn't nuke the topology. Persistence: **`STORAGE.TOPOLOGY_DRAFT`** auto-saves on every change (drop, move, cable, delete) so accidental reload never loses work; **`STORAGE.TOPOLOGIES`** holds up to 5 named saves with FIFO eviction by `updated` timestamp when the 6th is added; **Save As** prompts for a name and upserts by topology id; **Load** dropdown rebuilds from saves with device-count badges; **New** prompts to confirm if the canvas has devices. Mobile nudge: viewport < 900px width shows a friendly "Topology Builder works best on desktop" callout with an "Open Anyway" override that sets `tbMobileOverride = true` and continues. Builder state is prefixed `tb*` (tbState, tbSelectedId, tbPendingCableFrom, tbDragging, tbPaletteDrag, tbMobileOverride, tbCanvasHandlersAttached, tbKeyHandlerAttached) to avoid collision with the existing PBQ `topoDevices`/`selectedTopoDevice` state used by the drag-into-zones question type. | v4.15 | **Port Drill: Secure Pairs mode (#30)** ŌĆö fourth Port Drill mode joining Timed/Endless/Family. Dedicated drill for the Network+ secureŌåöinsecure protocol pairings (HTTPŌåöHTTPS, FTPŌåöFTPS/SFTP, TelnetŌåöSSH, SMTPŌåöSMTPS/587, LDAPŌåöLDAPS, POP3ŌåöPOP3S, IMAPŌåöIMAPS). New `nextPortPairsQ()` randomizes between two question formats: **port-pick** ("HTTPS is the secure version of HTTP. Which port does HTTPS use?") and **proto-pick** ("Which protocol replaces FTP (port 21) over SSH?"). Distractors come from the secure/insecure pool, deduped by the answered field, with the sibling protocol excluded so users never have to choose between two technically-correct answers. Timeless like family mode ŌĆö one wrong answer ends the streak.
